<h3><a name="page-1137200">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 001)</a></h3>

<p>1</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1886 June 11, Special Meeting.'>1886 <u>June 11, Special Meeting.</u></span></p>
<p><u>June 11. 1886.</u></p>
<p>A special meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held, as notified, on Friday, June 11, 1886<span class='line-break'> </span>at 11:30 o'clock, A. M.</p>
<p>Present:  the President and Messrs. Choate, <span class='line-break'> </span>Browne, Wolcott, Hodges, Clapp and Jones.</p>
<p>The records of the meeting of April 7.<span class='line-break'> </span>and of subsequent meetings were read and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sales of Land '><u>Sales of Land </u></span></p>
<p>The Secretry presented Statements of <span class='line-break'> </span>Sales of Land from April 7 to June 9.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives Lots #948 #4604'><u>Representatives Lots #948 #4604</u></span></p>
<p>Voted,.  That Representatives be designated <span class='line-break'> </span>for Lots, as follows:</p>
<p>Walter F. Osgood,  Newtonville  Son</p>
<p>Alfred S. Sanborn  Boston  Son</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had exam<span class='line-break'></span>ined and approved the Schedule of Monthly <span class='line-break'> </span>Bills, of May 12. $6457.96, and that the same <span class='line-break'> </span>had been thereupon paid by the Treasurer.</p>
<p>The Schedule of June 9. showing a total of <span class='line-break'> </span>$7622.54  was presented.</p>
<p>Voted That upon approval by the President, <span class='line-break'> </span>payment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Release Confirmed'><u>Release Confirmed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted.  That the Release executed in the name <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation by its Treasurer to Henrietta <span class='line-break'> </span>L. T. Wolcott, dated April 7, 1886, and recorded<span class='line-break'> </span>with Suffolk Deeds, lib. 1718, fol. 376, of a certain</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1137202">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 002)</a></h3>

<div id="page-1137204">
<h3><a name="page-1137204">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 003)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>003</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Petition of A. McDonald &amp; Co.'><u>Petition of A. M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Co.</u></span></p>
<p>A petition <sup>252</sup> was presented from Norman <span class='line-break'> </span>M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Co. for leave to set, from time to <span class='line-break'> </span>time, in Lots under perpetual care, such Mon<span class='line-break'></span>uments and Tablets as they might be called <span class='line-break'> </span>to set by the Proprietors of said Lots, permmis<span class='line-break'></span>sion to be first asked by the Proprietor, as <span class='line-break'> </span>in all other cases, such work to be done<span class='line-break'> </span>under such restrictions are the Board might <span class='line-break'> </span>deem proper.</p>
<p>Voted.  That the matter be referred to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Lots, with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Neglected Lots'><u>Neglected Lots</u></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Voted.  That Lots <sup>253</sup> numbered 1083. D. E. Chase,<span class='line-break'> </span>2316, Joseph Brooks, 2687, Nathaniel Evans, <span class='line-break'> </span>Jr., and 2822, Cynthia L. Rich, being in a <span class='line-break'> </span>state of continued neglect, and their con<span class='line-break'></span>dition impairing the appearance of athe <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery,the Secretary, under the direction <span class='line-break'> </span>of the President, send written notice by mail <span class='line-break'> </span>to the last known residence of the Proprietor <span class='line-break'> </span>or Representative of each of said Lots, of the <span class='line-break'> </span>fact of their condition, and that, if the same <span class='line-break'> </span>shall remain in such neglected condition for <span class='line-break'> </span>thirty days after the date of such notice the <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent put the same in proper order,<span class='line-break'> </span>under the direction of the President at the ex<span class='line-break'></span>pense of the respective Proprietors, as provided <span class='line-break'> </span>by Article VL of the By-Laws</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137206">
<h3><a name="page-1137206">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 004)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Chapel, Improvements in'><u>Chapel, Improvements in</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the Committee on Grounds <span class='line-break'> </span>employ some suitable person to consider <span class='line-break'> </span>what improvements are necessary in the <span class='line-break'> </span>Chapel, at the cemetery and to make an <span class='line-break'> </span>estimate of the cost of the same;  also</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Water Supply'><u>Water Supply</u></span></p>
<p>Voted.  That the Committee on Grounds <span class='line-break'> </span>consider the subject of the Water Supply <span class='line-break'> </span>at the Cemetery, and report.</p>
<p>Dissolved</p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1886 July 14 No. Quorum'><u>1886 July 14 No. Quorum</u></span></p>
<p><u>July 14. 1886</u></p>
<p>The monthly meeting was notified to <span class='line-break'> </span>be held on Wednesday, July 14. 1886 at <span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 P.M.</p>
<p><u>No quorum was present</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer.</p>
<p>Secretary</p>

<div id="page-1137210">
<h3><a name="page-1137210">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 006)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>006</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1886Nov. 10. Meeting'>1886<u>Nov. 10. Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>November 10. 1886</u></p>
<p>The monthly meeting of the Board of <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees was held as notified on Wednesday.<span class='line-break'> </span>November 10. 1886, at 2:30 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President, and Messrs Choate, <span class='line-break'> </span>Browne, Rice, Hodges, Wolcott, Sears, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Whitney, Clapp and Jones,</p>
<p>The records of the special meeting of June 11,<span class='line-break'> </span>and of subsequent meetings were read and <span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='N. McDonald &amp; Co. Petition refused'><u>N. M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Co. Petition refused</u></span></p>
<p>The President stated, on behalf of the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Lots, to whom was referred the matter <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Petition <sup>252</sup> of N. M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Co., for leave to<span class='line-break'> </span>set Monuments &amp;c. in Lots under perpetual <span class='line-break'> </span>care, that such permission had been refused <span class='line-break'> </span>and that the privilege formerly enjoyed by <span class='line-break'> </span>Alexander M<sup>c</sup>Donald had been revoked.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had ex<span class='line-break'></span>amined and approved the Schedules of <span class='line-break'> </span>Monthly Bills: July 14, $7,357.93;  August 11,<span class='line-break'> </span>$5,535.95; September 8, $6,437.83;  October 13, $7,655.57;<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the same had been thereupon paid <span class='line-break'> </span>by the Treasurer,.</p>
<p>The Schedule of November 10, showing a <span class='line-break'> </span>total of $5,606.80, was presented, and it was</p>
<p>Voted - that upon approval by the President <span class='line-break'> </span>payment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>The Secretry presented Statements of <sup>256.257.258.259.260</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Sales of Land from June 9 to November 10.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives Lot Nos.'><u>Representatives Lot Nos.</u></span></p>

Boston  Husband<span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1542'><u>1542</u></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Caroline M. Sister<span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='3191'><u>3191</u></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Edward S. Gordon  Boston  Newphew<span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='4035'><u>4035</u></span><span class='line-break'> </span>Edward B. Bayley  Boston.  Son.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Old Office Release'><u>Old Office Release</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the Treasurer be authorized to <span class='line-break'> </span>execute and deliver a release to the City of <span class='line-break'> </span>Boston of all claim for damages costs, expenses<span class='line-break'> </span>and compensation on account of the taking <span class='line-break'> </span>by the said city of the building No. 16 Pemberton <span class='line-break'> </span>Square, in which the offices of the Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>were then located;  it appearing that the <span class='line-break'> </span>lease to the corporation provided that, in <span class='line-break'> </span>case of such a taking by the City, no dam<span class='line-break'></span>ages should be Claimed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Water Supply'><u>Water Supply</u></span><span class='line-break'> </span>===<u>Chapel</u></p>
<p>The President stated, in behalf of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Grounds that they were not <span class='line-break'> </span>prepared to report in regard to the iprove<span class='line-break'></span>ment of the Chapel or upon the subject of <span class='line-break'> </span>Water Supply for the Cemetery; but, for the in<span class='line-break'></span>formation of the  Board he submitted an <span class='line-break'> </span>offer <sup>261</sup> made by B. F. Smith for sinking driven <span class='line-break'> </span>wells.  No action was taken thereon.</p>

<div id="page-1137216">
<h3><a name="page-1137216">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 009)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>009</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sstone Farm Offer.'><u>Sstone Farm Offer.</u></span></p>
<p>The President read a letter <sup>262.</sup> from Joshua C <span class='line-break'> </span>Stone, offering his land adjoining the Ceme<span class='line-break'></span>tery for $24,000, and also referred to a previous <span class='line-break'> </span>offer from the same person, December 3. 1883.<span class='line-break'> </span>No action was taken thereon</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Thomas Gray Lot Petition-'><u>Thomas Gray Lot Petition</u>-</span></p>
<p>A petition<sup>263.</sup> was presented from Mrs. Alice T. <span class='line-break'> </span>Almy, asking that Lot No. 670, formerly <span class='line-break'> </span>owned by her father, Thomas Gray, deceased, <span class='line-break'> </span>might be placed in her name as trustee,<span class='line-break'> </span>and a protest against any transfer of <span class='line-break'> </span>said Lot signed by Mrs. Henry and her <span class='line-break'> </span>mother, Mary S. Gray was also presented.<span class='line-break'> </span>Both were ordered to be placed on file.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Roland Litchfield Lot Contract'><u>Roland Litchfield Lot Contract</u></span></p>
<p>A proposition was received from the Executor<span class='line-break'> </span>of the estate of the late Roland Litchfield <span class='line-break'> </span>to pay a sum sufficient to brick up all <span class='line-break'> </span>interments already made in the single cham<span class='line-break'></span>ber tomb on the lot owned by deceased, #2443. -<span class='line-break'> </span>and to seal up in the same manner all <span class='line-break'> </span>subsequent interments, such since being addition<span class='line-break'></span>al to that named in the contract approved <span class='line-break'> </span>by the Board, June 11. 1886.</p>
<p>Voted,  that the Committee on Lots be authorized to <span class='line-break'> </span>make such a contract as they should deem proper<span class='line-break'> </span>in the premises.   Dissolved,<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis F. Farmer, Secy.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137218">
<h3><a name="page-1137218">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 010)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>10<span class='line-break'> </span><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1886'>1886</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1886 Dec. 8. No Quorum'>1886 <u>Dec. 8. No Quorum</u></span></p>
<p><u>December 8. 1886.</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting was notified to be <span class='line-break'> </span>held on Wednesday, December 8. 1886. at 2:30<span class='line-break'> </span>o'clock P.M,.</p>
<p><u>No quorum was present.</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer, <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1887January 12. Meeting.'>1887<u>January 12. Meeting.</u></span></p>
<p><u>January 12. 1887</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held as notified on Wednesday, January<span class='line-break'> </span>12. 1887. at 2:30 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present.  The President, and Messrs. Whitney, Rice, <span class='line-break'> </span>Eaton, Browne, Hodges, Wolcott, Sears, Clapp, Jones<span class='line-break'> </span>and Choate.</p>
<p>The records of the meetings of November 10. and <span class='line-break'> </span>December 8. were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Annual Reorts:'><u>Annual Reorts:</u></span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='President'><u>President</u></span></p>
<p>The President presented and read the Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>Report <sup>264</sup> to the Proprietors, and it was voted: -<span class='line-break'> </span>that the Annual Report, as read, be approved <span class='line-break'> </span>and adopted as the Report of the Trustees to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors, and that it be printed and distributed <span class='line-break'> </span>to the Proprietors.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>The Treasurer and Superintendent, having <span class='line-break'> </span>presented their respective Annual Reports <sup>265.266</sup>. it was</p>
</div>

<p><u>February 16. 1887.</u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held as notified, on Wednesday, February 16.<span class='line-break'> </span>1887. at 2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present.  The President and Messrs. Payson, Sears, <span class='line-break'> </span>Choate, Whitney, Hodges, Wolcott, Rice and Jones.</p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read and <span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 7.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 7.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that, at the Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting of the Proprietors held February 7. 1887,<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. William S. Eaton and Roger Wolcott were <span class='line-break'> </span>chosen Trustees for the term of Six Years, ending 1893.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it ap<span class='line-break'></span>peared that teh whole number of ballots cast was <span class='line-break'> </span>Seven, all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he <span class='line-break'> </span>was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer Superintendent and Secretary'><u>Treasurer Superintendent and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number for Treasurer, eight; all of which <span class='line-break'> </span>were for H. B. Mackintosh;  for Superintendent eight;<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for J. W. Lovering; whole number for <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary, eight; all of which were for L. G. Farmer; and <span class='line-break'> </span>each of the three last named were declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.  Treasurer  Assistant  Secretary  Superintendent'><u>Salaries fixed.  Treasurer  Assistant  Secretary  Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>Voted.  That the Salary of the Treasurer be fixed at <span class='line-break'> </span>$2.500 for the ensuing year;  that of his assistant at <span class='line-break'> </span>$1100; and that of the Secretary at $600; and that of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Superintendent, at $3200, and that he shall have <span class='line-break'> </span>the use of a House and the grounds thereto be<span class='line-break'></span>longing, the use of a Horse and Vehicle and the</p>
</div>

<p>19</p>
<p>that, if the same shall remain in such neglected <span class='line-break'> </span>condition for thirty days after the date of such <span class='line-break'> </span>notice, the Superintendent put them in proper <span class='line-break'> </span>order, under the direction of the President, at the <span class='line-break'> </span>expense of the respective Proprietors, as provided <span class='line-break'> </span>by Article VI of the By-Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Roland Litchfield Lot.'><u>Roland Litchfield Lot.</u></span></p>
<p>A communication was received from the <span class='line-break'> </span>executor of the estate of the late Roland <span class='line-break'> </span>Litchfield,enclosing a check for $500, a contract <span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual care of Lot No. 2443, owned <span class='line-break'> </span>by said deceased, in his lifetime, and a recon<span class='line-break'></span>veyance of said Lot to the Corporation in trust.<span class='line-break'> </span>The said contract not being in the form of a ap<span class='line-break'></span>proved by the Board at its meeting held June <span class='line-break'> </span>11, 1856, it was voted, that the said check <span class='line-break'> </span>contract and reconveyance be returned to <span class='line-break'> </span>said executor and that the whole matter be<span class='line-break'> </span>referred to the Committee on Lots, in accordance<span class='line-break'> </span>with the vote of the Board passed at its meeting <span class='line-break'> </span>held November 10, 1886.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Jos. S. Fay Request.'><u>Jos. S. Fay Request.</u></span></p>
<p>A request was presented from Joseph S. Fay,<span class='line-break'> </span>esq., Vice President of the Home for Little Wanderers,<span class='line-break'> </span>for a gift, or a sale at a nominal price, of a <span class='line-break'> </span>Lot to that instituion, and it was voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>that the Board had no power to grant said re<span class='line-break'></span>quest, and that the same be refused.</p>
<p>Dissolved  Lewis G. Farmer, Sec'y.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contract Bowditch Statue Vote of Thanks.'><u>Contract Bowditch Statue Vote of Thanks.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted That the thanks of the Board be <span class='line-break'> </span>presented to J. Ingersoll Bowdieth, Esq., for<span class='line-break'> </span>his generous gift of the re-casting of the <span class='line-break'> </span>bronze Statue of his father, the late Nathaniel <span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch;  also,</p>
<p>Voted, That the President and Treasurer be <span class='line-break'> </span>authorized to sign the following Contract <sup>275.</sup>for<span class='line-break'> </span>the preservation, and perpetual care of said Statue:</p>
<p>"  Memorandyum of Agreement made this <span class='line-break'> </span>8th. day of July, A. D. 1887.  between the Proprietors <span class='line-break'> </span>of Mt. Auburn Cemetery and J. Ingersoll Bow<span class='line-break'></span>ditch: The said Bowditch having this day <span class='line-break'> </span>paid to the Treasurer of said Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>the sum of Two Hundred dollars, the Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>hereby agrees to invest the said sum, and use <span class='line-break'> </span>the yearly income thereof for cleaning the bronze <span class='line-break'> </span>Statue of Dr. Nathaniel Bowditch now in the grounds <span class='line-break'> </span>of said Corporation by brushign the same twice</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137244">
<h3><a name="page-1137244">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 023)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>23</p>
<p>a year; but in no event is the Statue ever to be <span class='line-break'> </span>painted, or cleaned by the use of pumice stone,<span class='line-break'> </span>or in any other way or manner except only by <span class='line-break'> </span>brushing.</p>
<p>In Witness Whereof the Corporation has caused <span class='line-break'> </span>its common seal to be hereto affixed and these p[?]<span class='line-break'> </span>ents to be excuted by the President and Treasurer, <span class='line-break'> </span>hereto duly authorized, and the said J. Ingersoll <span class='line-break'> </span>Bowditch has hereto set his hand and seal on <span class='line-break'> </span>the day and year first above written,</p>
<p>Dissolved.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p>October 27, 1887.</p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held, as notified, on Thursday, October 27,<span class='line-break'> </span>1887, at 12 o'clock, M.</p>

<p>The records of the meeting of September<span class='line-break'> </span>23 were read and approved.</p>

<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills of October <span class='line-break'> </span>12, was presented, showing a total of $8,951.40:<span class='line-break'> </span>Voted, that upon approval by the President, <span class='line-break'> </span>payment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer&apos;s Quarterly Report'><u>Treasurer's Quarterly Report</u></span></p>
<p>The Treasurer having presented his Report<sup>276</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>for the Quarter ending September 20, 1887.  the <span class='line-break'> </span>same ws referred to the Committee on Finance.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1137246">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 025)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>25</p>
<p>Elizabeth T. Lyon, 2440, Theo. Gulbranson, 2862, <span class='line-break'> </span>Louis Turner, [?]3838, Mrs. Matilda Richardson <span class='line-break'> </span>being in a state of continued neglect, and their <span class='line-break'> </span>condition impairing the appearance of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>tery, the Secretary, under the direction of the <span class='line-break'> </span>President, send written notice by mail to the <span class='line-break'> </span>last known residence of the Proprietor or Rep<span class='line-break'></span>resentative of each of said Lots, of the fact<span class='line-break'> </span>of their condition, and that if the same shall <span class='line-break'> </span>remain in such neglected condition for thirty<span class='line-break'> </span>days after the date of such notice, the Super<span class='line-break'></span>intendent put them in proper order, under the <span class='line-break'> </span>direction of the President, at the expense of the <span class='line-break'> </span>respective Proprietors, as provided by Article <span class='line-break'> </span>VI of the By-Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sewer assessment Mt. Auburn Street.'><u>Sewer assessment Mt. Auburn Street.</u></span></p>
<p>The President presented to the Board for their <span class='line-break'> </span>consideration the matter of the assessment laid upon <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery by the City of Cambridge on account of <span class='line-break'> </span>the constrution of the sewer in Mr. Auburn Street,<span class='line-break'> </span>and after discusion it was voted that the whole<span class='line-break'> </span>subject be referred to the President and Messrs. Choate<span class='line-break'> </span>and Whitney as a Committee, with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='[?] J. Johnson Petition Lot #5816.'><u>[?] J. Johnson Petition Lot #5816.</u></span></p>
<p>A Petition <sup>278</sup> was presented from [?] J. John<span class='line-break'></span>son, owner of Lot No. 5816, for leave to erect a Headstone<span class='line-break'> </span>thereon, of a height greater than that allowed by the con<span class='line-break'></span>ditions of the deed of said Lot, but the Board adjourned with<span class='line-break'></span>out taking action thereon.  Dissolved<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer, Secretary.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 8.1888.'><u>February 8.1888.</u></span></p>
<p><u>February 8. 1888.</u></p>
<p>The monthly meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held as notified on Wednesday, February 8.<span class='line-break'> </span>1888. at 2:30 o'clock  P.M.</p>
<p>Present.  The President and Messrs Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Hodges, Jones, Rice, Sears and Wolcott.</p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read <span class='line-break'> </span>and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 6. 1888.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 6. 1888.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting of the Proprietors held February 6. 1888.<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs Samuel R. Payson and T. Quincy Browne<span class='line-break'> </span>were chosen Trustees for the term of Six years, ending 1894.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it <span class='line-break'> </span>appeared that the whole number of ballots cast <span class='line-break'> </span>was seven, all of which were for Israel M.<span class='line-break'> </span>Spelman, and he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer, Superintendent and Secretary'><u>Treasurer, Superintendent and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number for Treasurer, seven, all of <span class='line-break'> </span>which were for H. B. Mackintosh;  for Super<span class='line-break'></span>intendent, seven, all of which were for J. W. <span class='line-break'> </span>Lovering; for Secretary, seven, all of which were <span class='line-break'> </span>for L. G. Farmer; and each of the three last <span class='line-break'> </span>named was declared elected.</p>
<p>===<u>Salaries Treasurer  Assistant  Secretary  Superintendent</u>---</p>
<p>Voted, that the salary of the Treasurer be <span class='line-break'> </span>fixed at $2,500 for the ensuing year;  that of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Assistant at $1,200;  that of the Secretary at $600;<span class='line-break'> </span>and that of the Superintendent at $3,200, and <span class='line-break'> </span>that he shall have the use of a House and the <span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Offices for Corporation'><u>Offices for Corporation</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the President and Messrs Choate<span class='line-break'> </span>and Browne be constituted a Committee to <span class='line-break'> </span>consider the subject of obtaining permanent <span class='line-break'> </span>office for the Corporation.</p>
<p>Dissolved.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Cambridge Sewer Assessment'><u>Cambridge Sewer Assessment</u></span></p>
<p>Voted - That the Treasurer be authorized to<span class='line-break'> </span>execute the following agreement on behalf<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation: -</p>
<p>"Whereas the Proprietors of the Cemetery of<span class='line-break'> </span>Mount Auburn have filed in the Supreme</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Rond.'><u>Rond.</u></span></p>
<p>Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk a<span class='line-break'> </span>petition for a writ of certiorare, seeking to<span class='line-break'> </span>quash certain proceedings of the Mayor and<span class='line-break'> </span>Aldermen of the City of Cambridge in</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137258">
<h3><a name="page-1137258">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 037)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>37</p>
<p>assessing to the Mt Auburn Cemetery Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration upon certain land, part of said<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery, a part of the cost of a sewer on Mount<span class='line-break'> </span>Auburn Street, and to enjoin William W. Dal<span class='line-break'></span>linger, treasurer of said City from selling said <span class='line-break'> </span>land;</p>
<p>and Whereas said Proprietors desire that the<span class='line-break'> </span>said City shall not seek to enforce said assess<span class='line-break'></span>ment by sale of said land, pending proceed<span class='line-break'></span>ings upon said petition, and at the termina<span class='line-break'></span>tion of said proceedings the lieu of the City<span class='line-break'> </span>upon said land will probably have expired;</p>
<p>Now, therefore, the said Proprietors hereby agree<span class='line-break'> </span>that if the City of Cambridge shall refrain from<span class='line-break'> </span>taking any steps toward the sale of said land<span class='line-break'> </span>pending said petition for certiorare, and if the<span class='line-break'> </span>Court shall determine that said City had a <span class='line-break'> </span>right by virtue of said proceedings of the Mayor<span class='line-break'> </span>and Aldermen to enforce said assessment against<span class='line-break'> </span>said Proprietors by sale of said lands or any<span class='line-break'> </span>thereof, or if said Proprietors shall abandon said<span class='line-break'> </span>petition, said Proprietors will pay to said City the<span class='line-break'> </span>amount so assessed with interest thereon within<span class='line-break'> </span>30 days after the termination of proceedings upon<span class='line-break'> </span>said petition"</p>
<p>Dissolved.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 13. Meeting.'><u>February 13. Meeting.</u></span></p>
<p><u>February 13, 1889.</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held as notified on Wednesday, February 13,<span class='line-break'> </span>1889, at 2:30 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Choate,<span class='line-break'> </span>Brown, Jones Wolcott, Hodges, Eaton, Rice and<span class='line-break'> </span>Whitney.</p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 4 1889.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 4 1889.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting of the Proprietors held February 4, 1889,<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Henry A. Rice and Channing Clapp<span class='line-break'> </span>were chosen Trustees for the term of Six years, end<span class='line-break'> </span>ing 1895.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election -of- President.'><u>Election -of- President.</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it<span class='line-break'> </span>appeared that the whole number of ballots cast<span class='line-break'> </span>was five, all of which were for Israel M. Spel<span class='line-break'></span>man, and he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer Superintendent and Secretary'><u>Treasurer Superintendent and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots for Treasurer, seven,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for Su<span class='line-break'></span>perintendent, seven, all of which were for J.<span class='line-break'> </span>W. Lovering; for Secretary, six, all of which were<span class='line-break'> </span>for L.G. Farmer; and each of the three last named<span class='line-break'> </span>was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.'><u>Salaries fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted. that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed<span class='line-break'> </span>at $2,500 for the ensuing year; that of the Assist<span class='line-break'></span>and at $1,200; that of the Secretary at $600; and<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>that of the Superintendent at $3,200, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the last named shall have the use of<span class='line-break'> </span>a House and the grounds thereto belonging,<span class='line-break'> </span>the use of a horse and vehicle, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>services of one man at the expense of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committees continued.'><u>Committees continued.</u></span></p>

<p>all respects.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Land of Coolidge Heris Purchase of.'><u>Land of Coolidge Heris Purchase of.</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported on behalf of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots to whom was referred the matter of the pur<span class='line-break'></span>chase of land on Grove Street, Watertown, formerly<span class='line-break'> </span>belonging to the late John Coolidge, that they had<span class='line-break'> </span>purchased of James H. Coolidge, Lot No. 6 on a Plan<span class='line-break'> </span>of the estate of said John Coolidge, recorded with<span class='line-break'> </span>Middlesex South District Deeds, Plan Book 57. p.42,<span class='line-break'> </span>containing about 278,100 square feet, at a cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>$4,550.77; and it was thereupon, -</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Purchase Confirmed'><u>Purchase Confirmed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the report be accepted, and the action<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Committee ratified and adopted in all<span class='line-break'> </span>respects, and also that the said committee be<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized to make such further purchases<span class='line-break'> </span>of land adjoining said lot so purchased as<span class='line-break'> </span>they shall deem expedient.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation'><u>Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President then gave notice, in accordance with<span class='line-break'> </span>Article IX. of the By Laws, that, at the next meeting of<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board, he should ask for an appropriation to an<span class='line-break'> </span>amount exceeding $1,000. to be expended in making</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137275">
<h3><a name="page-1137275">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 054)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>54</p>
<p>such further purchases.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Brattle St. Widening.'><u>Brattle St. Widening.</u></span></p>
<p>The subject of the proposed widening of Brattle<span class='line-break'> </span>Street by the City of Cambridge in accordance with the<span class='line-break'> </span>order of April 23, 1889, was presented, and it was -</p>
<p>Voted, that the matter of widening Brattle Street and<span class='line-break'> </span>the settlement with the City of Cambridge for damages  <span class='line-break'> </span>in consequence of the same be referred to the Commit<span class='line-break'></span>tee on Lots, with full powers.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Greenhouse for Tropical Plants'><u>Greenhouse for Tropical Plants</u></span></p>
<p>The President then stated that it appeared from<span class='line-break'> </span>a plan presented by the Superintendent that said<span class='line-break'> </span>widening of Brattle Street, if carried out as pro<span class='line-break'></span>posed would necessitate the removal of one of<span class='line-break'> </span>the greenhouses and it was thereupon</p>
<p>Voted, that the Committee on Lots be authorized<span class='line-break'> </span>to construct a new greenhouse, as a cost not<span class='line-break'> </span>exceeding $3500, whenever, in their judgment,<span class='line-break'> </span>it shall seem desirable so to do, and also to<span class='line-break'> </span>make such other alterations as may be rendered<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary in consequence.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropri-ation.'><u>Notice of Appropri-ation.</u></span></p>
<p>The President then gave notice, in accordance<span class='line-break'> </span>with Article IX of the By-Laws, that, at the next<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of the Board, he should ask for an ap<span class='line-break'></span>propriation to an amount exceeding $1000, to be ex<span class='line-break'></span>pended for this purpose.</p>
<p>Dissolved,<span class='line-break'> </span>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<p>Voted, That the report be accepted and the<span class='line-break'> </span>action of the President ratified and confirmed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Caroline J. Hill Request Lot 2337.'><u>Caroline J. Hill Request Lot 2337.</u></span></p>
<p>A communication was received from Carolin J.<span class='line-break'> </span>Hill, owner of Lot No. 2337, on Bellwork Patch, asking<span class='line-break'> </span>that the Board of Trustees would authorize the division<span class='line-break'> </span>of the same into two separate lots, each containing<span class='line-break'> </span>630 square feet, and numbered as shown upon a<span class='line-break'> </span>plan thereof made by the Superintendent and an<span class='line-break'></span>nexed to said communication; and it was</p>
<p>Voted, That the subject be referred to the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Lots, with full power.</p>
<p>Dissolved,<span class='line-break'> </span>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secretary&apos;s Oath'><u>Secretary's Oath</u></span></p>
<p>Commonwealth of Massachusetts.<span class='line-break'> </span>Suffolk, ss. Boston, February 12, 1890.</p>
<p>Personally appeared Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>and made oath that he would faithfully dis<span class='line-break'></span>charge the duties of Secretary of the Proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, before me,</p>
<p>Jerome Jones.<span class='line-break'> </span>Justice of the Peace.</p>

<div id="page-1137295">
<h3><a name="page-1137295">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 074)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>74</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report'><u>Report</u></span></p>
<p>services of the officers of the Corporation in administering said<span class='line-break'> </span>fund, reported verbally that in view of the necessirty of main<span class='line-break'> </span>taining a surplus of the Repair Fund to meet unforseen<span class='line-break'> </span>contingencies, and of the present reduced rate of interest<span class='line-break'> </span>as compared with that formerly received, the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>did not deem it advisable to make any change in the<span class='line-break'> </span>method of anministering the same. The Committee,<span class='line-break'> </span>however, recommended that, as the surplus of the Repair<span class='line-break'> </span>Fund appeared to be fully sufficient for present pur<span class='line-break'> </span>poses, the sum of $1708.40, with interest compounded<span class='line-break'> </span>at 4 percent, be transferred from that fund to the<span class='line-break'> </span>General Fund, from which it was transferred to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Repair Fund by vote of the Board of Trustees, passed<span class='line-break'> </span>December 10, 1873.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Vote'><u>Vote</u></span></p>
<p>Upon motion, the report of the Committee was ac<span class='line-break'></span>cepted, and the transfer ordered to be made, as rec<span class='line-break'></span>ommended.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Plan of Cemetery'><u>Plan of Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>The President on behalf of the Committee on Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>to whom was referred, at the meeting of February 12, the<span class='line-break'> </span>subject of preparing a new outline Plan of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery Grounds, as suggested at the last Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting, presented a copy of the existing^305^Plan,<span class='line-break'> </span>with the recent changes and additions sketched<span class='line-break'> </span>thereon, as prepared by the Superintendent, and re<span class='line-break'></span>ported that the old plate could be altered at small<span class='line-break'> </span>expense so as to show such changes and additions,<span class='line-break'> </span>and recommended the same to the Board for their</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1137296">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 075)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>75</p>
<p>adoption.</p>
<p>Voted. That the Committee on Lots be authorized to<span class='line-break'> </span>cause such alterations to be made in the plate, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>Ten Thousand copies of the same be printed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Catalogue'><u>New Catalogue</u></span></p>
<p>The President, on behalf of the Committee on Lots, to<span class='line-break'> </span>whom was referred, at the meeting of February 12, the<span class='line-break'> </span>subject of preparing a new Catalogue<sup>306</sup>of the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>read a communication from the Superintendent in<span class='line-break'> </span>regard to the New Catalogue and Plan, and presented<span class='line-break'> </span>several specimen proof sheets showing an alphabet<span class='line-break'></span>ical list of the proprietors and also an arrangement<span class='line-break'> </span>of Lots by paths and numbers, with estimates of cost.</p>
<p>After some discussion, it was Voted -</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Vote.'><u>Vote.</u></span></p>
<p>That the Committee on Lots be authorized to prepare<span class='line-break'> </span>a new Catalogue in the form shown in style No. 3, con<span class='line-break'></span>taining a list of Trustees and officers, an alphabeti<span class='line-break'></span>cal list of proprietors and an alphabetical list of ave<span class='line-break'></span>nues and paths, under which the lot numbers and<span class='line-break'> </span>names of proprietors are to be entered in regular order:<span class='line-break'> </span>the same to be printed in double columns; and that<span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee be authorized to cause Five Thousand<span class='line-break'> </span>copies of the same to be printed, of which 2500 shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be found in cloth, the new Plan of the Cemetery to</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Rescinded part. Sup. 82'><u>Rescinded part. Sup. 82</u></span></p>
<p>be bound in each copy: and, further, that a statement<span class='line-break'> </span>be included in the next Annual Report to the effect<span class='line-break'> </span>that any proprietor may obtain one of the cloth-bound<span class='line-break'> </span>copies upon application at the office of the Corporation</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137297">
<h3><a name="page-1137297">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 076)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>76</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Record of Undivided Interests in Lots.'><u>Record of Undivided Interests in Lots.</u></span></p>
<p>The President, on behalf of the Committee ap<span class='line-break'></span>pointed at the meeting of February 12, to appear be<span class='line-break'></span>fore the House Committee on the Judiciary, in oppo<span class='line-break'></span>sition to the petition of Lowell M. Palmer and others<span class='line-break'> </span>for legislation to compel the making of records of<span class='line-break'> </span>conveyances of undivided interests in Lots, and<span class='line-break'> </span>for securing to holders of such undivided interests<span class='line-break'> </span>their rights of burial reported that the members<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Committee had attended the hearing before<span class='line-break'> </span>the Judiciary Committee, and that the arguments<span class='line-break'> </span>against the petition were presented by Mr Choate;<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the Judiciary Committee reported at a<span class='line-break'> </span>later day, giving the petitioners leave to withdraw.</p>
<p>Dissolved</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='July 9. No Quorum'><u>July 9. No Quorum</u></span></p>

<p><u>No quorum was present.</u></p>

<h3><a name="page-1137298">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 077)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='July 14 /Special Meeting'><u>July 14 /Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>July 14. 1890</u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held, as notified on Monday, July 14. 1890,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 12:15 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present.  The President and Messrs. Browne, Eaton<span class='line-break'> </span>Jones, Rice, Whitney and Wolcott.</p>
<p>The reading of the records of the last meeting <span class='line-break'> </span>was waived.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Water Pipe for Cemetery'><u>Water Pipe for Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>Voted.  That the President and Superintednent be <span class='line-break'> </span>authorized to make a contract for such iron water<span class='line-break'></span>pipe as may be needed for use in the Cemetery, not<span class='line-break'> </span>exceeding one milethereof, and report at the <span class='line-break'> </span>next meeting of the  Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation'><u>Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President gave notice that at the next meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing of the Board he should ask for an appropri<span class='line-break'></span>ation not exceeding $8000 for the purpose of paying <span class='line-break'> </span>for such water pipe.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Transfer for Repair to General Fund Vote'><u>Transfer for Repair to General Fund Vote</u></span></p>
<p>On motion of Mr. Browne it was voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>That the vote of the Board passed at the meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing of June 19. transferring the sum of $1708.40 and <span class='line-break'> </span>interest from the Repair Fund with the General  Fund <span class='line-break'> </span>be rescinded.</p>
<p>Dissolved,<span class='line-break'> </span>L. G. Farmer, <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary<span class='line-break'> </span>That the</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><u>November 12, 1890.</u></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of July 14, 1890, and of<span class='line-break'> </span>subsequent meetings were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined<span class='line-break'> </span>and approved the Schedules of Monthly Bills: -</p>

<p>Voted, that the action of the President in this regard<span class='line-break'> </span>be fully ratified and approved.</p>
<p>The Schedule of November 12, showing a total of<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>$</sup>5,824.45, was presented, and it was thereupon -</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Plan of Cemetery.'><u>Plan of Cemetery.</u></span></p>

<p>had completed the Abstract of Deeds, and had <span class='line-break'> </span>been paid the sum of $1000 as compensation there<span class='line-break'></span>for, as provided by vote of the Board, passed  <span class='line-break'> </span>January 14. 1870.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Water Pipes AppropriationSee page 77'><u>New Water Pipes Appropriation</u>See page 77</span></p>
<p>Voted, that the sum of $8000. be appropriated to <span class='line-break'> </span>defray the expense of putting the new iron water<span class='line-break'> </span>pipes into the Cemetery, the same to be expended <span class='line-break'> </span>under the direction of the President; and</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Repair Fund to be charged 1/2 of expense.'><u>Repair Fund to be charged 1/2 of expense.</u></span></p>
<p>that, whereas the system of water works in <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery is largely for the purpose of <span class='line-break'> </span>keeping in good order the Lots under the perpetual <span class='line-break'> </span>care of the Corporation, one-half of the ex<span class='line-break'></span>pense of putting in said new water pipes be <span class='line-break'> </span>charged to the Repair Fund.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Greenhouse'><u>New Greenhouse</u></span></p>
<p>Te President presented plans and estimates<span class='line-break'> </span>for the construction of a new greenhouse for <span class='line-break'> </span>bedding plants to take the lace of hot-beds, and</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation'><u>Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>gave notice that at the next meeting of the Board<span class='line-break'> </span>he should ask for an appropriation exceeding $1000 for this purpose.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Water Pipes'><u>New Water Pipes</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that the work of <span class='line-break'> </span>laying new water pipes in the Cemetery had so far <span class='line-break'> </span>progressed favorably, and stated that to complete<span class='line-break'> </span>the water works it would be necessary to lay about <span class='line-break'> </span>2000 feet more of eight-inch pipe from the engine <span class='line-break'> </span>house through Citron, Birch, Cherry and Eagle <span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues to Magnolia Avenue, and gave notice</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation'><u>Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>that at the next meeting of the Board he should <span class='line-break'> </span>ask for an appropriation exceeding $1000. for this <span class='line-break'> </span>purpose.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer, <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p><u>February 11</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held, as notified, on Wednesday, February 11, 1891<span class='line-break'> </span>at 2:30 o'clock P.M.<span class='line-break'> </span>Present. the President and Messrs. Browne Choate<span class='line-break'> </span>Eatou, Hodges, Jones, Whitney and Wolcott. <span class='line-break'> </span>The records of the last meeting were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees'><u>Trustees</u></span>The President announced that at the Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>{elected} Meeting of the Proprietors held February 2, 1891, Messrs. <span class='line-break'> </span>{Feb. 2, 1891} David R. Whitney and Richard M. Hodges were chosen <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to serve for the term of six years ending 1897. <span class='line-break'> </span>{Election} A ballot having been taken for President it ap<span class='line-break'></span>{of} peared that the whole number of ballots cast was<span class='line-break'> </span>{Presiden} seven all of which were for Israel M. Belwau; and <span class='line-break'> </span>he was declared elected. Whole numbers of bal<span class='line-break'></span>{Treasurer} lots cast for Treasurer, eight, all of which were for <span class='line-break'> </span>{Superintendent} H.B. Machintosh, for Superintendent, eight, all of <span class='line-break'> </span>{and} which were for J.W. Lousring; and for Secretary, <span class='line-break'> </span>{Secretary} eight, all of which were for L.G. Faruer; and <span class='line-break'> </span>they were severally, declared elected. <span class='line-break'> </span>{Salaries} Voted. that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed<span class='line-break'> </span>{fixed} at $2500 for the ensuing year; that of the Assistant<span class='line-break'> </span>at $1200; that of the Secretary at $600, and that he be <span class='line-break'> </span>allowed the use of the office without paymentt [ofract?]<span class='line-break'> </span>therefor; and that of the Superintendant at 3600, and that <span class='line-break'> </span>the last-named shall have the use of a House and the <span class='line-break'> </span>grounds thereto belonging, the use of a Horse and Vehicle</p>

<h3><a name="page-1137309">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 088)</a></h3>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='George T. Curtis Request.'><u>George T. Curtis Request.</u></span></p>
<p>A Communication^318^was presented from Mr. George<span class='line-break'> </span>Ticknor Curtis, stating that he had been notified by<span class='line-break'> </span>the Superintendent that the remains of his child which<span class='line-break'> </span>had been deposited in the Receiving Tomb, would be re<span class='line-break'></span>moved therefrom unless the fees amounting to <sup>$</sup>60. were<span class='line-break'> </span>paid before August 1, 1891; and requesting that the time<span class='line-break'> </span>for such payment be extended to September 15, 1891, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>one-half of the amount of said fees be remitted.</p>
<p>Voted, that the subject be referred to the President<span class='line-break'> </span>with full power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='N.J. Bradlee Transfer from Lot 2083 to Lot 4397 $75.'><u>N.J. Bradlee Transfer from Lot 2083 to Lot 4397 <sup>$</sup>75.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, to authorize the transfer of <sup>$</sup>75. from the amount<span class='line-break'> </span>paid for the perpetual care of Lot No. 2083, formerly owned<span class='line-break'> </span>by the late Nathaniel J. Bradlee, for the purpose<span class='line-break'> </span>of providing for the perpetual care of the three Head<span class='line-break'> </span>stones recently removed from said Lot No. 2083 and erected<span class='line-break'> </span>upon said Lot No. 4397. Dissolved.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1892'>1892</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='January 18 Special Meeting'><u>January 18 Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>January 18, 1892.</u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held as notified on Monday, January 18, 1892, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:15 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Choate, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Jones, Rice, Sears and Wolcott.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of September 28, 1892, and<span class='line-break'> </span>of subsequent meetings were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Channing Clapp Resignation'><u>Channing Clapp Resignation</u></span></p>
<p>The resignation of Mr. Channing Clapp as a mem<span class='line-break'></span>ber of the Board of Trustees was accepted and his<span class='line-break'> </span>letter of resignation was placed on file.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved the following Schedules of Monthly Bills: -</p>
<p>October 14, <sup>$</sup>6,774.06; November 11, <sup>$</sup>4,618.08; December 9,<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>$</sup>3,906.52; and that payments of the same had<span class='line-break'> </span>been made by the Treasurer accordingly.</p>
<p>The Schedule of January 13, 1892, showing a total<span class='line-break'> </span>of <sup>$</sup>5,086.71, was presented, and it was thereupon</p>
<p>Voted, That upon approval thereof by the Pres<span class='line-break'></span>ident, payment be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Annual Reports, President'><u>Annual Reports, President</u></span></p>
<p>The President having presented and read the An<span class='line-break'></span>nual Report^319^to the Proprietors, it was</p>
<p>Voted, That the same be approved and adopted as<span class='line-break'> </span>the Annual Report of the Trustees to the Proprietors,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that it be printed and distributed to them ac<span class='line-break'></span>cordingly.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer'><u>Treasurer</u></span></p>
<p>The Report^320^of the Treasurer as approved by the</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>102</p>
<p>the appearance of the Cemetery, the Secretary, under<span class='line-break'> </span>the direction of the President, send written notice by<span class='line-break'> </span>mail to the last known residence of the Proprietor or<span class='line-break'> </span>Representative of each of said Lots, of the fact of their<span class='line-break'> </span>condition; and that if the same shall remain in such<span class='line-break'> </span>neglected condition for thirty days after the date of such<span class='line-break'> </span>notice, the Superintendent put them in proper order,<span class='line-break'> </span>under the direction of the President, at the expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of the respective Proprietors, as provided by Article<span class='line-break'> </span>VI. of the By-Laws.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secretary&apos;s Oath'><u>Secretary's Oath</u></span></p>

<p>Personally appeared Lewis G. Farmer<span class='line-break'> </span>and made oath that he would faithfully discharge<span class='line-break'> </span>the duties of Secretary of the Proprietors of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn, before me,</p>
<p>Jerome Jones.<span class='line-break'> </span>Justice of the Peace.</p>

<div id="page-1137324">
<h3><a name="page-1137324">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 103)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>103</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1892'>1892</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 10. Meeting.'><u>February 10. Meeting.</u></span></p>
<p><u>February 10, 1892.</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees was held,<span class='line-break'> </span>as notified, on Wednesday, February 10, 1892, at 2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Browne, Choate, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Johnson, Jones, Rice, Sears and Wolcott.</p>
<p>Voted, to waive reading the records of the last meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 1, 1892.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 1, 1892.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual Meeting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietors held February 1, 1892, Messrs. Israel M. Spelman<span class='line-break'> </span>and Jerome Jones were chosen Trustees to serve for the term of<span class='line-break'> </span>six years, ending 1898, and that Mr. Samuel Johnson was<span class='line-break'> </span>chosen Trustee for the unexpired term of Mr. Channing<span class='line-break'> </span>Clapp, resigned, ending 1895.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it appeared<span class='line-break'> </span>that the whole number of ballots was eight, all of<span class='line-break'> </span>which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he was declared<span class='line-break'> </span>elected.  Whole number of ballots cast for Treasurer,</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer.'><u>Treasurer.</u></span></p>
<p>nine, all of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for Super-</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Superintendent'><u>Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>intendent, nine, all of which were for J.W. Lovering; and</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='and Secretary'><u>and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>for Secretary, nine, all of which were for L.G. Farmer; and<span class='line-break'> </span>they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed'><u>Salaries fixed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>$</sup>2500 for the ensuing year; that of the Assistand at <sup>$</sup>1200;<span class='line-break'> </span>that of the Secretary at <sup>$</sup>600, and that he be allowed the<span class='line-break'> </span>use of the office without payment of rent therefor; and<span class='line-break'> </span>that of the Superintendent at <sup>$</sup>3600, and that the last<span class='line-break'></span>named shall have the use of a House and the grounds<span class='line-break'> </span>thereto belonging, the use of a Horse and Vehicle, and<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p>104</p>
<p>the services of one Man at the expense of the Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Standing Committees'><u>Standing Committees</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced the Standing Committees<span class='line-break'> </span>for 1892-1893, as follows:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Grounds'><u>Grounds</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Grounds.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>The President, ex officio, and Messrs. Choate, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Jones and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lots'><u>Lots</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Lots</u><span class='line-break'> </span>The President and Messrs. Jones and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Finance'><u>Finance</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Finance</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Browne and Wolcott.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Interments.'><u>Interments.</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Interments.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Hodges and Johnson.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills.'><u>Monthly Bills.</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills for February 10,<span class='line-break'> </span>was presented, showing a total of <sup>$</sup>3,636.04; and it <span class='line-break'> </span>was voted that upon approval by the President,<span class='line-break'> </span>payment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='March 9 No Quorum'><u>March 9 No Quorum</u></span></p>

<p>A special meeting of the Board of Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>was held, as notified on Thursday, June 9. 1892,<span class='line-break'> </span>at 12:30 o'clock. P. M.</p>
<p>Present, the President, and Messrs. Browne,<span class='line-break'> </span>Choate, Eaton, Johnson, Jones, Payson and Wolcott.</p>

<p>The President reported that he had examined <span class='line-break'> </span>and approved the following Schedules of Monthly Bills:<span class='line-break'> </span>March 9, $3,129.37;  April 13. $3,724.99;  and May 11,<span class='line-break'> </span>$7,396.55, and that the same had been thereupon <span class='line-break'> </span>paid by the Treasurer.  Voted.  That the action <span class='line-break'> </span>of the President in this regard be fully ratified <span class='line-break'> </span>and approved.</p>

<div id="page-1137347">
<h3><a name="page-1137347">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 126)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>126</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1893'>1893</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='December 28. Special Meeting'><u>December 28. Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>December 28, 1893.</u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held, as notified, on Thursday, December 28, 1893, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Browne,<span class='line-break'> </span>Choate, Eaton, Hodges, Jones, Rice, Sawyer, Sears<span class='line-break'> </span>and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records read'><u>Records read</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of May 17, 1893, and<span class='line-break'> </span>of subsequent meetings were read and approved</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills.'><u>Monthly Bills.</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined<span class='line-break'> </span>and approved the following schedules of<span class='line-break'> </span>Monthly Bills: June 14, <sup>$</sup>7300.96; July 12, <sup>$</sup>7078.40;<span class='line-break'> </span>August 9, <sup>$</sup>6785.80; September 13, <sup>$</sup>5973.58; October<span class='line-break'> </span>11, <sup>$</sup>7273.28; November 8, <sup>$</sup>4679.20; December 13, <sup>$</sup>4901.87;<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the same had been thereupon paid<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Treasurer. Voted, That the action<span class='line-break'> </span>of the President in this regard be fully rat<span class='line-break'></span>ified and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer&apos;s Quarterly Reports.'><u>Treasurer's Quarterly Reports.</u></span></p>
<p>The Treasurer having presented his Reports^331, 332.^<span class='line-break'> </span>for the Quarters ending June 30, and September 30,<span class='line-break'> </span>respectively, the same were referred to the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Finance.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Bird Estate Appropriation Voted.'><u>Bird Estate Appropriation Voted.</u></span></p>
<p>In accordance with the notice given at the meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing of May 17, 1893, the President asked for an ap<span class='line-break'></span>prication of <sup>$</sup>2000. for the purchase of the Bird estate,<span class='line-break'> </span>lying between the Westerly side of the Cemetery and<span class='line-break'> </span>land of the Fitchburg Railroad Company.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137348">
<h3><a name="page-1137348">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 127)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>127</p>
<p>Voted That the sume of Two Thousand dollars (<sup>$</sup>2000.) be<span class='line-break'> </span>appropriated for that purpose.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Railroad Tracks on-'><u>Railroad Tracks on-</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that the Fitchburg Railroad<span class='line-break'> </span>Company had laid a track upon the Bird estate, at<span class='line-break'> </span>an expense to the Corporation of <sup>$</sup>440, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>same had proved itself a great convenience in the<span class='line-break'> </span>matter of the supply of gravel and other materials.</p>

<p>129</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Guidebook'><u>New Guidebook</u></span></p>
<p>The President presented to the Trustees copies<span class='line-break'> </span>of the new Guidebook, prepared under vote of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Board, December 14, 1892.</p>
<p>===<u>Petition of J.A.B. Cutter</u></p>
<p>A communication^333^was received from John A.B.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cutter, as king for authority to remove the remains of<span class='line-break'> </span>his brother, from Lot No. 3498, standing in the name<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation in Trust, the purpose of re<span class='line-break'></span>moval being to re-inter said remains in the Na<span class='line-break'></span>tional Cemetery, at Arlington. Voted that the<span class='line-break'> </span>request be granted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Petition of Horace D. Litchfield &amp; others'><u>Petition of Horace D. Litchfield &amp; others</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^334^was presented from Horace D.<span class='line-break'> </span>Litchfield and others asking leave to remove<span class='line-break'> </span>from Lot NO. 2443, standing in the name of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation in Trust, the remains of the late Pro<span class='line-break'></span>prietor, Roland Litchfield, for the purpose of re-in<span class='line-break'></span>terning the same in the Cambridge Cemetery, where his<span class='line-break'> </span>widow is also buried. Voted that the matter be<span class='line-break'> </span>referred to the Committee on Lots, with power.</p>
<p>Dissolved. L.G. Farmer, Sec'y.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='January 10 No Quorum'><u>January 10 No Quorum</u></span></p>
<p>The monthly meeting was notified to be held on Wednesday, Jan. 10, 1894, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 o'clock P.M. <u>No quorum was present.</u> L.G. Farmer, Sec'y.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1894'>1894</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Jan. 22 Special Meeting'><u>Jan. 22 Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>January 22, 1894.</u></p>
<p>A special meeting of the Board of Trustees was held,<span class='line-break'> </span>as notified, on Monday, January 22, 1894, at 2:30 o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Browne, Choate,<span class='line-break'> </span>Eaton, Johnson, Jones, Rice, Sawyer and Shaw.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved the schedule of Monthly Bills for January 10,<span class='line-break'> </span>1894, amounting to <sup>$</sup>3,424.28, and that the same had been<span class='line-break'> </span>thereupon paid by the Treasurer. Voted that the action<span class='line-break'> </span>of the President in this regard to be fully ratified and approved</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives appointed'><u>Representatives appointed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that Representatives be designated for Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>as follows: -</p>
<p><sup>#</sup>695. Charles B. Cummings, of Boston, Son.<span class='line-break'> </span>3626. Georgianna W. Meacham of Dover, Mass., Widow.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Annual Reports'><u>Annual Reports</u></span></p>
<p>The President having presented and read the<span class='line-break'> </span>^335^Annual Report to the Proprietors, it was</p>
<p>Voted that the same be approved and adopted as</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='President'><u>President</u></span></p>
<p>the Annual Report of the Trustees to the Proprietors,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that it be printed and distributed to them ac<span class='line-break'></span>cordingly.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>The Report of the Treasurer^336^, as approved by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Finance, and that of the Superintendent^337^</p>
<p>Voted, that the same be accepted, printed and<span class='line-break'> </span>distributed to the Proprietors.</p>

<p>Voted, that the Treasurer, Henry B. Mackintosh, be, and he hereby<span class='line-break'> </span>is, authorized and empowered in the name and on behalf of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, to sign, seal with the corporate seal, execute, acknowl<span class='line-break'></span>edge and deliver a release from the operation of a certain mort<span class='line-break'></span>gage given by Horace B. and Henrietta M. Parker to said Corpora<span class='line-break'></span>tion, dated August 22, 1889, and recorded with Middlesex South<span class='line-break'> </span>District Deeds, Lib. 1928. fol. 4, upon payment to him of the<span class='line-break'> </span>sum of One dollar, two certain parcels of land situated in<span class='line-break'> </span>Newton, and more particularly described in said release; one<span class='line-break'> </span>containing 14250 square feet, and the other containing 6661 sq.<span class='line-break'> </span>feet.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Partial Release of Wise Mortgage'><u>Partial Release of Wise Mortgage</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Treasurer, Henry B. Mackintosh, be and he hereby <span class='line-break'> </span>is, authorized and empowered, in the name and on behalf of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, to sign, seal with the corporate seal, execute, acknowl<span class='line-break'></span>edge and deliver a release from the operation of a certain mort<span class='line-break'></span>gage given by Charles H. Wise and Frances A. Wise to said Corp<span class='line-break'></span>oration, dated COtober 22, 1892, and recorded with Suffolk Deeds,<span class='line-break'> </span>Lib. 2091, fol. 348, upon payment to him of the sum of Twenty<span class='line-break'></span>five Hundred dollars (<sup>$</sup>2500.), on account of the principal sum<span class='line-break'> </span>named in said Mortgage, a stip of land bounded by Poplar,<span class='line-break'> </span>Washington and Ashland streets, containing 5228 square feet,<span class='line-break'> </span>and being the same premises taken from said Francis A. Wise<span class='line-break'> </span>by a Resolve and Order of the Board of Street Commissioners<span class='line-break'> </span>of the City of Boston, for the widening of said Poplar Street,<span class='line-break'> </span>passed Dec. 8, 1893.</p>
<p>Dissolved</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer, Secretary<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1137353">
<h3><a name="page-1137353">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 132)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>132</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1894'>1894</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 14, Meeting'><u>February 14, Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u>February 14, 1894.</u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held as notified, on Wednesday, February 14, 1894, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Choate, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Johnson, Rice, Sawyer, Sears, Shaw and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records read'><u>Records read</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 5, 1894.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 5, 1894.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting of the Proprietors, held February 5, 1894, Messrs.<span class='line-break'> </span>J. Quincy Browne and Joseph Sawyer were re-elected<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to serve for the term of six years, ending 1900.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it ap<span class='line-break'></span>peared that the whole number of ballots cost was<span class='line-break'> </span>seven, all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and<span class='line-break'> </span>he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer'><u>Treasurer</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cost for Treasurer, nine,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for Superin-</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Superintendent and Secretary'><u>Superintendent and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>tendent, nine, all of which were for J.W. Lovering; and<span class='line-break'> </span>for Secretary, nine, all of which were for L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>and they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.'><u>Salaries fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Salary of the Treasurer be fixed<span class='line-break'> </span>at <sup>$</sup>2500 for the ensuing year; that of the assistant<span class='line-break'> </span>at <sup>$</sup>1500; that of the Secretary at <sup>$</sup>600, and that he be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed the use of the office without payment of rent<span class='line-break'> </span>therefor; and that of the Superintendent at <sup>$</sup>4000, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the last-named shall have the use of a House</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137354">
<h3><a name="page-1137354">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 133)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>133</p>
<p>and the grounds thereto belonging, the use of a Horse<span class='line-break'> </span>and Vehicle and the services of one Man at the expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Standing Committees.'><u>Standing Committees.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced the Standing Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittees for 1894-5, as follows: -</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Grounds'><u>Grounds</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Grounds</u><span class='line-break'> </span>The President, ex officio, and Messrs. Choate, Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>Jones and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lots'><u>Lots</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Lots.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>The President and Messrs Jones and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Finance'><u>Finance</u></span></p>
<p><u>Committee on Finance</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Browne and Shaw.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Interments'><u>Interments</u></span></p>
