<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills for February 14,<span class='line-break'> </span>was presented, showing a total of <sup>$</sup>3376.83; and it was<span class='line-break'> </span>voted that upon approval by the President, payment<span class='line-break'> </span>thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>

<p>Voted, that Representatives designated for Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>as follows: -</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Neglected Lots'><u>Neglected Lots</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that Lots^338^numbered 2059, Cottle, and 2235,<span class='line-break'> </span>Porter, being in a state of continued neglect, and their<span class='line-break'> </span>condition impairing the appearance of the Cemetery, the<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary, under the direction of the President, send written<span class='line-break'> </span>notice by mail to the last known residence of the Proprietor</p>

<div id="page-1137355">
<h3><a name="page-1137355">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 134)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>134</p>
<p>or Representative of each of said Lots, of the fact<span class='line-break'> </span>of their condition; and that if the same shall remain<span class='line-break'> </span>in such neglected condition for thirty days after the date<span class='line-break'> </span>of such notice, the Superintendent put them in proper<span class='line-break'> </span>order, under the direction of the President, at the expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of the respective proprietors, as provided by Article VI.<span class='line-break'> </span>of the By-Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='J.M. Sears Gift of Lot for Ornamental Purposes.'><u>J.M. Sears Gift of Lot for Ornamental Purposes.</u></span></p>
<p>Mr. Joshua M. Sears having stated that by the<span class='line-break'> </span>purchase of the Fremont House property some years<span class='line-break'> </span>ago, he had come into possession of Lot No. 324, sit<span class='line-break'></span>uated on Chestnut Avenue and containing 300 square<span class='line-break'> </span>feet, originally purchased by the Fremont House pro<span class='line-break'></span>prietors, and that, not desiring to use the same, he<span class='line-break'> </span>wished to convey it to the Corporation to be used for<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamental purposes only, for which its location ren<span class='line-break'></span>dered it particularly desirable, it was Voted, that the<span class='line-break'> </span>gift of said Lot on the part of Mr. Sears, be accepted<span class='line-break'> </span>in behalf of the Corporation, the same to be used for orna<span class='line-break'></span>mental purposes only.</p>
<p>On motion of Mr. Johnson, seconded by Mr. Eaton,<span class='line-break'> </span>it was further voted that the thanks of the Corpora<span class='line-break'></span>tion be tendered to Mr. Sears for his generous gift.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sidewalk Assessment and Grade Damages Mt. Auburn St.'><u>Sidewalk Assessment and Grade Damages Mt. Auburn St.</u></span></p>
<p>for their consideration the matter of the assess<span class='line-break'></span>ment laid upon the Cemetery by the City of Cambridge<span class='line-break'> </span>on account of the construction of a sidewalk along<span class='line-break'> </span>the line of the Cemetery on Mt. Auburn Street, and<span class='line-break'> </span>also the matter of a claim of the Corporation for<span class='line-break'> </span>damages sustained by it by reason of the changing<span class='line-break'> </span>of grade and raising of the sidewalk on said street,<span class='line-break'> </span>it was Voted, that the whole subject be referred<span class='line-break'> </span>to the President and Messrs. Choate and Whitney<span class='line-break'> </span>as a Committee with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contracts Perpetual Care'><u>Contracts Perpetual Care</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Lots reported the follow<span class='line-break'></span>ing Contracts for Perpetual Care, all of which<span class='line-break'> </span>were approved by the Board:</p>
<p><sup>#</sup>983 *Sarah O. Proctor by Ex'r. <sup>$</sup>550.<span class='line-break'> </span>3415 George N. Phelps 450.<span class='line-break'> </span>3911 Corporation in Trust (add'l) 50.<span class='line-break'> </span>4141 *Margaret A. Sargent by Ex'r. 500.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Annual Report to Proprietors'><u>Annual Report to Proprietors</u></span></p>
<p>The Annual Report^342^of the President was<span class='line-break'> </span>presented and read by the President. The same<span class='line-break'> </span>contained an amendment, as proposed, of the third<span class='line-break'> </span>clause of Article VIII. of the By Laws, and upon con<span class='line-break'></span>sideration by the Board, it was voted that the proposed</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Amendment to By-Laws'><u>Amendment to By-Laws</u></span></p>
<p>amendment be presented in the following form to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors fo rtheir sanction:</p>
<p>"All such sums shall collectively constitute a sep<span class='line-break'></span>"arate fund, called the 'Repair Fund,' and shall be in<span class='line-break'></span>"vested in the public debt of the United States, or in that<span class='line-break'> </span>"of the State of Massachusetts, or in the debt of any of the<span class='line-break'> </span>"counties, cities, or towns of this State, or in mortgages of<span class='line-break'> </span>"real estate in any city or town in Massachusetts.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer&apos;s Quarterly Report'><u>Treasurer's Quarterly Report</u></span></p>
<p>The Treasurer having presented his Report^345^for<span class='line-break'> </span>the quarter ending March 31, 1895, the same was<span class='line-break'> </span>referred to the Committee on Finance.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Front Entrances'><u>New Front Entrances</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that after considering the<span class='line-break'> </span>subject of arranging new front entrances to the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery which was, at the meeting of the Board held on<span class='line-break'> </span>July 10, 1894, referred to himself and the Superintend<span class='line-break'></span>ent, with power, and after spending much time on<span class='line-break'> </span>plans for improvement, the Committee had concluded<span class='line-break'> </span>that they were not warranted in expending so much<span class='line-break'> </span>money as would be necessary to construct two new en<span class='line-break'></span>trances in Keeping with the Egyptian style of architect<span class='line-break'></span>ure of the present front entrance, and that it would</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137376">
<h3><a name="page-1137376">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 155)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>155</p>
<p>be better to open a new gateway at some future time in<span class='line-break'> </span>the Northwest corner of the Cemetery opposite the Fitch<span class='line-break'></span>burg Railroad Station and to put in order the gateway<span class='line-break'> </span>at the corner of Coolidge Avenue, thus affording ad<span class='line-break'></span>dditional means for entrance and exit for carriages when<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary; but that nothing should be done at present.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Death of Mr. Lovering'><u>Death of Mr. Lovering</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that Mr. James W. Lov<span class='line-break'></span>ering who had fille dthe office of Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery for nearly a quarter of a century,<span class='line-break'> </span>had died form the effects of his injuries received<span class='line-break'> </span>on May 10 in being thrown from his buggy while<span class='line-break'> </span>driving in the Cemetery in the discharge of his<span class='line-break'> </span>duty. The President detailed the circum<span class='line-break'></span>stances of the accident as far as the same<span class='line-break'> </span>had been ascertained, and inquired what<span class='line-break'> </span>action the Board would take in the case.<span class='line-break'> </span>After discussion the following votes were<span class='line-break'> </span>passed:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Resolutions'><u>Resolutions</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, "That we deeply regreat the loss of our late<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent, James W. Lovering, by accidental<span class='line-break'> </span>death, and the sudden termination of his long<span class='line-break'> </span>period of twenty-three years service in the employ<span class='line-break'></span>ment of this Corporation, during which he distin<span class='line-break'></span>guished himself by his ability, high character, and<span class='line-break'> </span>devotion to our interests"</p>
<p>Voted "That the salary of the Superintendent to<span class='line-break'> </span>October 1 next be paid to his widow for her use and</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137377">
<h3><a name="page-1137377">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 156)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>156</p>
<p>that of her children, and that she be allowed to<span class='line-break'> </span>occupy the house and grounds to July 1. next, with<span class='line-break'> </span>the services of one man to keep the grounds in order."</p>
<p>Voted, "That we sincerely sympathize with his be<span class='line-break'></span>reaved family in their affliction and that the Secre<span class='line-break'></span>tary be directed to transmit to them a copy of these<span class='line-break'> </span>votes as our testimonial to his character and worth<span class='line-break'> </span>and our appreciation of his valuable services."</p>
<p>Voted, also, that the President be allowed to continue<span class='line-break'> </span>the use of the house and grounds to Mr. Lovering's<span class='line-break'> </span>family for a longer period if, in his judgment,<span class='line-break'> </span>it should be consistent with the interests of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation so to do.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committee to select new Sup&apos;t.'><u>Committee to select new Sup't.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the President and Messrs. Choate<span class='line-break'> </span>and Jones be appointed a Committee to select<span class='line-break'> </span>a new Superintendent and report.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><u>June 14, 1895.</u></p>

<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Browne,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cheever, Choate, Foster, Johnson, Jones, Sawyer and<span class='line-break'> </span>Shaw.</p>

<p>The President reported that he had examined<span class='line-break'> </span>and approved the Schedule of Monthly Bills of<span class='line-break'> </span>June, 12, 1895, amounting to <sup>$</sup>9,880.13, and that pay<span class='line-break'></span>ment had been thereupon made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p>Voted, that the action of the President in<span class='line-break'> </span>this regard be fully ratified and approved.</p>

<p>100 W. Newton St.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1137379">
<h3><a name="page-1137379">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 158)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>158</p>
<p>a state of continued neglect, and its condition im<span class='line-break'></span>pairing the appearance of the Cemetery, the Secretary,<span class='line-break'> </span>under the direction of the President, send written notice<span class='line-break'> </span>by mail to the last known residence of the Proprietor, of<span class='line-break'> </span>the fact of its condition; and that if the same shall<span class='line-break'> </span>remain in such neglected condition for thirty days after<span class='line-break'> </span>the date of such notice, the Superintendent put it in<span class='line-break'> </span>proper order, under the direction of the President, at<span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietor's expense, as provided by Article VI. of<span class='line-break'> </span>the By-Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='James C. Scorgie elected Superintendent'><u>James C. Scorgie elected Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported, on behalf of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>appointed at the meeting of May 24, last, to select<span class='line-break'> </span>a new Superintendent, that the matter had received<span class='line-break'> </span>careful consideration and the Committee had de<span class='line-break'></span>cided to report the name of James C. Scorgie, the<span class='line-break'> </span>present Assistant Superintendent as the candidate<span class='line-break'> </span>for Superintendent. The report of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>was accepted and, upon motion, a ballot was<span class='line-break'> </span>taken, at which nine votes were cast, all of <span class='line-break'> </span>which were for James C. Scorgie and he was duly<span class='line-break'> </span>declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salary fixed.'><u>Salary fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Salary of the Superintendent be<span class='line-break'> </span>fixed at <sup>$</sup>2500, and be payable at that rate, begin<span class='line-break'></span>ning July 1 next; that he shall have the use of a<span class='line-break'> </span>House and the Grounds thereto belonging, the use of a<span class='line-break'> </span>Horse and Vehicle and the services of one Man, at<span class='line-break'> </span>the expense of the Corporation.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137380">
<h3><a name="page-1137380">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 159)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>159</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Letter from Mrs. Lovering'><u>Letter from Mrs. Lovering</u></span></p>
<p>A letter^346^was read from Mrs. Lovering acknowl<span class='line-break'></span>edging the receipt of the resolutions adopted by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board upon the death of her late husband, and<span class='line-break'> </span>upon motion, the same was placed on file.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Bicycles in Cemetery'><u>Bicycles in Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>A communication^347^from Mr. Benjamin Vaughan,<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor of Lot No. 4892 was presented by the<span class='line-break'> </span>President and read, in which the writer requested<span class='line-break'> </span>that a permit might be granted to him to enter<span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery upon a bicycle. After full dis<span class='line-break'></span>cussion it was voted, that the Secretary, under the<span class='line-break'> </span>direction of the President, be authorized to issue yearly<span class='line-break'> </span>passes to Proprietors of lots, to enter the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>upon a bicycle, under the following conditions: -</p>
<p>1. The bicycle to be used upon Avenues only.<span class='line-break'> </span>2. The rate of speed not to exceed 5 miles an hour<span class='line-break'> </span>3. No "coasting" to be indulged in.<span class='line-break'> </span>4. The rider in no case to pass a funeral pro<span class='line-break'></span>cession or near to any Lot where funeral exercises<span class='line-break'> </span>are taking place, unless he shall be dismounted.<span class='line-break'> </span>5. The pass to be shown whenever used.<span class='line-break'> </span>6. The pass to be cancelled upon a violation<span class='line-break'> </span>of any one of the above conditions.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer authorized to make entry upon Mortgaged Premises'><u>Treasurer authorized to make entry upon Mortgaged Premises</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Treasurer be, and he hereby is,<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized and empowered to enter, on behalf o fthe<span class='line-break'> </span>corporation, upon any premises held in mortgages<span class='line-break'> </span>by it, for breach of condition of the mortgages,<span class='line-break'> </span>and to make and record all necessary or usual<span class='line-break'> </span>certificates and affidavits of such entry.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Grade Damages Settled'><u>Grade Damages Settled</u></span></p>
<p>The President, on behalf of the Committee appointed<span class='line-break'> </span>at the meeting of <date when='1894-10-04'>October 5, 1894</date>, to whom was referred<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter of the settlement of the claim of the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration for damages caused by the change in the grade<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mount Auburn street, reported that a settlement<span class='line-break'> </span>had been effected witht he City of Cambridge for<span class='line-break'> </span>Thirteen Hundred and Fifty dollars (<sup>$</sup>1350.) from which<span class='line-break'> </span>the sum of One Hundred and Seventy-five dollars (<sup>$</sup>175.)</p>

<p>164</p>
<p>for counsel fees and expenses was to be deducted,</p>
<p>Voted that the report of the Committee be accepted<span class='line-break'> </span>and the settlement ratified on behalf of the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Garden Ave. Grading Notice of Appropriation'><u>Garden Ave. Grading Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President then stated that it would be<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary to expend the net proceeds of the claim<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation for such grade damages, in<span class='line-break'> </span>raising the grade of Garden avenue and the<span class='line-break'> </span>Lots bordering thereon and near the same, and<span class='line-break'> </span>gave notice that at the next meeting he should<span class='line-break'> </span>ask for an appropriation equal to the amount of<span class='line-break'> </span>said net proceeds, for that purpose.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Petition of Louisa K. Wilson et al.'><u>Petition of Louisa K. Wilson et al.</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^351^was presented from Louisa K. Wilson<span class='line-break'> </span>and Sarah I. Kimball, children and sole heirs-at-law<span class='line-break'> </span>of Daniel Kimball, Jr., and as such proprietors of<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot No. 1640, praying that the same might be relo<span class='line-break'></span>cated and subdivided into two Lots, as shown on a<span class='line-break'> </span>plan annexed to said petition.</p>
<p>Voted, that the Secretary be instructed and author<span class='line-break'></span>ized to receive a reconveyance of said Lot to the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration and to deliver to said petitioners quite claim<span class='line-break'> </span>deeds of said two Lots so relocated, upon such con<span class='line-break'></span>ditions as may be imposed by the Committee on Lots</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Petition of Caroline E. Bonney'><u>Petition of Caroline E. Bonney</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^354^was presented from Caroline E. Bonney,<span class='line-break'> </span>praying that Lot No. 3821, owned by her might be<span class='line-break'> </span>relocated and subdivided into two Lots, as shown on a<span class='line-break'> </span>plan annexed to said petition.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Telephone at Cemetery'><u>Telephone at Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>The question of establishing telephone services<span class='line-break'> </span>at the Cemetery was presented and discussed<span class='line-break'> </span>and it was voted that the matter be referred to<span class='line-break'> </span>the President, with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Chapel'><u>New Chapel</u></span></p>
<p>The question of the advisability of erecting a<span class='line-break'> </span>New Chapel in the Cemetery was also presented<span class='line-break'> </span>and discussed and it was finally Voted that<span class='line-break'> </span>the whole subject be referred to a Committee to<span class='line-break'> </span>investigate and consider the same and report.</p>
<p>The President and Messrs. Choate and Sears<span class='line-break'> </span>were named as the Committee, and, on motion of Mr.<span class='line-break'> </span>Foster, Mr. Jones was added as a member thereof.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for President, it ap<span class='line-break'></span>peared that the whole number of ballots cast was ten,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he<span class='line-break'> </span>was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer'><u>Treasurer</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for Treasurer, ten,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for Superin-</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Superintendent and Secretary'><u>Superintendent and Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>tendent, ten, all of which were for James C. Scorgie;<span class='line-break'> </span>and for Secretary, ten, all of which were for L.G. <span class='line-break'> </span>Farmer, and they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed'><u>Salaries fixed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed<span class='line-break'> </span>at <sup>$</sup>2,500. for the ensuing year; that of the assistant<span class='line-break'> </span>at <sup>$</sup>1,500; that of the Secretary at <sup>$</sup>800, and that he be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed the use of the office without payment<span class='line-break'> </span>of rent therefor; and that of the Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>at <sup>$</sup>2,500; and that the last named shall have the use<span class='line-break'> </span>of a House and the grounds thereto belonging, the use<span class='line-break'> </span>of a Horse and Vehicle and the services of one Man, at<span class='line-break'> </span>the expense of the corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committees continued'><u>Committees continued</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that all Committees, having unfinished bus<span class='line-break'></span>iness in their hands be continued in office with the same<span class='line-break'> </span>powers as originally conferred upon them.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved the Schedule o fMonthly Bills of January 8,<span class='line-break'> </span>amounting to <sup>$</sup>2,811.03, and that payment of the same had<span class='line-break'> </span>been thereupon made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p>Voted, that the action of the President in this regard<span class='line-break'> </span>be fully ratified and approved.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #2941 Petition of Executors of Will of *N.P. Coburn.'><u>Lot <sup>#</sup>2941 Petition of Executors of Will of *N.P. Coburn.</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^356^was presented from James A. Woolson<span class='line-break'> </span>and others, Executors of the Will of Nathan P. Coburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>deceased, formerly owner of Lot No. 2941, which was re<span class='line-break'></span>conveyed by him to the Corporation in trust, represent<span class='line-break'></span>ing that after making such reconveyance, the deceased<span class='line-break'> </span>had married and left his widow surviving him, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>she desired to be interred in said Lot, in which there was<span class='line-break'> </span>sufficient room for the purpose, after providing for the<span class='line-break'> </span>interment of all persons designated in said reconvey<span class='line-break'></span>ance as entitled ot burial therein, and praying that<span class='line-break'> </span>the Board would permit such interment to be made.</p>
<p>Voted, that the assent of the Board be given to<span class='line-break'> </span>the making of such interment</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #4188 Petition of Trustees under will of Anne Patterson'><u>Lot <sup>#</sup>4188 Petition of Trustees under will of Anne Patterson</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^357^was presented from J. Theodore Heard<span class='line-break'> </span>and another, Trustees under the will of Anne Patterson,<span class='line-break'> </span>deceased, formerly owner of Lot No. 4188, asking that the<span class='line-break'> </span>contract made by them for the perpetual care of said<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot be so amended as to more distinctly provide for<span class='line-break'> </span>the renewal, when necessary, of the Monument and<span class='line-break'> </span>Headstones upon the Lot.</p>
<p>Voted, that the Secretary be authorized and instructed<span class='line-break'> </span>to so alter the said contract and the record thereof</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137394">
<h3><a name="page-1137394">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 173)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>173</p>
<p>as to provide in terms for the renewal, when neces<span class='line-break'></span>sary, of said Monument and Headstones.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Chapel - Report of Committee'><u>New Chapel - Report of Committee</u></span></p>
<p>The President, on behalf of the Committee appoint<span class='line-break'></span>ed at the meeting of the Board on <date when='1895-10-18'>October 18, 1895</date>, to<span class='line-break'> </span>consider and report upon the expendiency of erecting<span class='line-break'> </span>a New Chapel in the Cemetery, presented the following <span class='line-break'> </span>Report:</p>
<p>"The Committee have carefully examined into the con<span class='line-break'></span>dition of the present Chapel and have come to the con<span class='line-break'></span>clusion that, owing to its faulty construction, it cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>be adapted to the demands of the present time without<span class='line-break'> </span>such thorough reconstruction as would involve an ex<span class='line-break'></span>pense, nearly, if not quite, equal to the cost of a new build<span class='line-break'></span>ing. And, moreover, after the necessary additions and<span class='line-break'> </span>alterations are made, they are of the opinion that it is<span class='line-break'> </span>extremely doubtful whether a building on the limited<span class='line-break'> </span>site of the old Chapel would answer the present needs.</p>
<p>They have, therefore, concluded to recommend to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board the construction of a new Chapel, and at the same<span class='line-break'> </span>time, and in connection therewith a building for the<span class='line-break'> </span>offices of the corporation. The location of these buildings<span class='line-break'> </span>to be on or near the site of the present Well-House, near the<span class='line-break'> </span>front entrance, and the land thereto adjoining. By con<span class='line-break'></span>necting the two buildings, both can be more conveniently<span class='line-break'> </span>and economically heated and cared for. The estate now<span class='line-break'> </span>occupied on the opposite side of Mount Auburn Street can also<span class='line-break'> </span>be vacated and disposed of, and the proceeds of the sale</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137395">
<h3><a name="page-1137395">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 174)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>174</p>
<p>will, in part, defray the expense of the new buildings.,</p>
<p>This expense we have no means at present of estimating<span class='line-break'> </span>but we think it should not exceed Fifty Thousand dollars."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Vote'><u>Vote</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Report be accepted and that the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee be authorized to employ an architect, or architects, and<span class='line-break'> </span>obtain such plans, elevations and estimates of the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>the proposed new buildings as they shall judge necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>for submission to the Board for their decision.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secretary&apos;s Oath'><u>Secretary's Oath</u></span></p>
<p>Commonwealth of Massachusetts,</p>
<p>Suffolk, ss. Boston, <date when='1896-02-12'>February 12, 1896.</date></p>
<p>Personally appeared Lewis G. Farmer<span class='line-break'> </span>and made oath that he would faithfully and<span class='line-break'> </span>impartially discharge the duties of Secretary of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, before me</p>
<p>H.B. Mackintosh<span class='line-break'> </span>Justice of the peace.</p>
</div>

<p><sup>#</sup>3510. Paul F. Folsom, of Boston, Son.<span class='line-break'> </span>3568 Frances G. Black " Cambridge Widow<span class='line-break'> </span>3837 Russell A. Ballon " Newton Son.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Chapel Report'><u>New Chapel Report</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on the proposed New Chapel <span class='line-break'> </span>reported through the President, as chairman of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee, that after a careful examination of<span class='line-break'> </span>all the plans which had been sent for ap<span class='line-break'></span>proval, they had concluded to recommend for the<span class='line-break'> </span>acceptance of the Board, the plans and design<span class='line-break'> </span>presented by Mr. Willard T. Sears</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sears Plans adopted'><u>Sears Plans adopted</u></span></p>
<p>The plans were then examined by the Board<span class='line-break'> </span>and after full discussion it was voted, -</p>
<p>That the plans and design for a new office build<span class='line-break'></span>ing and Chapel, offered by Mr. Willard T. Sears Ar<span class='line-break'></span>chitect, be accepted; also, Voted,</p>
<p>That the Committee be authorized to construct<span class='line-break'> </span>the buildings substantially according to said plans, pro<span class='line-break'></span>vided they can be built by responsible contractors for<span class='line-break'> </span>the sum of Fifty Thousand dollars, which sum is<span class='line-break'> </span>not to include the architect's commission; also Voted,</p>
<p>That Messrs. J.R. Coolidge, Jr., Messrs. Longfellow,</p>
</div>

<p>Alden &amp; Harlow and T. Wilton Lewis, whose plans<span class='line-break'> </span>have not been accapted, be paid One Hundred dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>each for the same agreeably to understanding with<span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation'><u>Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Statues in Old Chapel'><u>Statues in Old Chapel</u></span></p>
<p>The subject of the disposition of the Statues in the<span class='line-break'> </span>Old Chapel was brought before the Board by the Pres<span class='line-break'></span>ident, who read an extract from Dr. Bigelow's History<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mount Auburn, giving the reasons for the selection<span class='line-break'> </span>of the subjects of the statues. They are of the following</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Subjects and Cost of Same'><u>Subjects and Cost of Same</u></span></p>
<p>persons and were executed by the following artists: -</p>
<p>Governor Winthrop by Richard S. Greenough.<span class='line-break'> </span>James Otis " Thomas Crawford.<span class='line-break'> </span>John Adams " Randolph Rogers.<span class='line-break'> </span>Judge Story " William W. Story.</p>
<p>For the three first named the sum of Five Thous<span class='line-break'></span>and dollars (<sup>$</sup>5,000.) each was appropriated by<span class='line-break'> </span>vote of the Corporation, while that of Judge Story<span class='line-break'> </span>was paid for by private subscription.</p>
<p>The items of cost and other expenses, as shown by the<span class='line-break'> </span>books of the Treasurer, including the cost of the bust of<span class='line-break'> </span>Dr. Bigelow and the labor etc., upon the erection o fthe<span class='line-break'> </span>statue of the Sphinx, were given as follows: -</p>
<p>Statue of John Adams <sup>$</sup>5,000.00<span class='line-break'> </span>Statue of Gov. Winthrop 5050.00<span class='line-break'> </span>Statue of James Otis 5050.00<span class='line-break'> </span>Pedestals, teaming, etc. 265.20<span class='line-break'> </span>Bust of Dr. Bigelow 668.75<span class='line-break'> </span>Labor and material placing Sphinx 1554.63</p>

<p>The fund for the Story Statue, being found in</p>

<div id="page-1137409">
<h3><a name="page-1137409">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 188)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>188</p>
<p>excess of the amount required, the balance, <sup>$</sup>990.97,<span class='line-break'> </span>was, by vote of the subscribers to the fund, passed to the<span class='line-break'> </span>credit of the Repair Fund, the income to be applied<span class='line-break'> </span>to the care of the Story Lot. The total amount of <span class='line-break'> </span>the subscriptions was <sup>$</sup>15,861.97.</p>
<p>After some informal discussion of the question of the<span class='line-break'> </span>removal of the statues to the New Chapel, it was voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>That the subject be laid on the table.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Petition of Edmund M. Wood Lot #3675.'><u>Petition of Edmund M. Wood Lot <sup>#</sup>3675.</u></span></p>
<p>A petition^362^was presented form Mr. Edmund M. Wood,<span class='line-break'> </span>asking permission to inter the remains of his infant<span class='line-break'> </span>granddaughter, Grace H. Wood in Lot No. 3675, which<span class='line-break'> </span>had been re-conveyed by himself and others to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation in trust, such interment not being a specif<span class='line-break'></span>ically provided for in such reconveyance.</p>
<p>Voted, that the subject be referred to the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Interments.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Receiving Tomb. Use of regulated.'><u>Receiving Tomb. Use of regulated.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that after a body has been once interred<span class='line-break'> </span>in the Cemetery, the same shall not be allowed to<span class='line-break'> </span>be placed in the Receiving Tomb, except upon the<span class='line-break'> </span>order of the Committee on Interments.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Widening of Mt. Auburn St. Counsel to be employed'><u>Widening of Mt. Auburn St. Counsel to be employed</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had retained coun<span class='line-break'></span>sel to attend the hearing before the County Commis<span class='line-break'></span>sioners on November 17, upon the question o fthe widen<span class='line-break'></span>ing of Mount Auburn Street, and to look after the<span class='line-break'> </span>interests of the Corporation in the matter.</p>
<p>Voted, that the action of the President in this re<span class='line-break'></span>gard be fully ratified and approved.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137410">
<h3><a name="page-1137410">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 189)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>189</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Organ and New Bell'><u>Organ and New Bell</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the matter of the purchase of an Organ<span class='line-break'> </span>for the New Chapel and also the question of<span class='line-break'> </span>the purchase of a New Bell be referred to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Building Committee, with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Appropriation for New Chapel'><u>Appropriation for New Chapel</u></span></p>
<p>The President, in accordance with the notice given<span class='line-break'> </span>at the meeting of June 26, asked for an additional<span class='line-break'> </span>appropriation of Fifteen Thousand dollars (<sup>$</sup>15,000.),<span class='line-break'> </span>to be expended in the erection of the New Office<span class='line-break'> </span>Building and Chapel, the same to be inclusive of<span class='line-break'> </span>architect's commissions, and it was accordingly</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Voted.'><u>Voted.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that said additional amount of Fifteen<span class='line-break'> </span>Thousand dollars (<sup>$</sup>15,000) be appropriated for that<span class='line-break'> </span>purpose.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Dec. 9 No Quorum'><u>Dec. 9 No Quorum</u></span></p>

<p><u>No quorum was present.</u></p>

<div id="page-1137413">
<h3><a name="page-1137413">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 192)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>192</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1897'>1897</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 10 Monthly Meeting'><u>February 10 Monthly Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1897-02-10'>February 10, 1897.</date></u>===</p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees was held,<span class='line-break'> </span>as notified, on Wednesday, February 10, 1897, at 2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Browne, Cheever, Foster,<span class='line-break'> </span>Johnson, Sawyer, Shaw and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the last meeting were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 1, 1897.'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 1, 1897.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that, at the Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Proprietors held <date when='1897-02-01'>February 1, 1897,</date> Messrs. David R.<span class='line-break'> </span>Whitney and David W. Cheever were chosen Trusteres, to<span class='line-break'> </span>serve for six years, ending 1903.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President.'><u>Election of President.</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a President,<span class='line-break'> </span>it appeared that the whole number of ballots cast was<span class='line-break'> </span>6, all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he was<span class='line-break'> </span>declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for a Treasurer, 7, all<span class='line-break'> </span>of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for a Secretary, 7, all<span class='line-break'> </span>of which were for L.G. Farmer; and for a Superintendent,<span class='line-break'> </span>8, all of which were for James C. Scorgie; and they were<span class='line-break'> </span>severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.'><u>Salaries fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at <sup>$</sup>2,500.<span class='line-break'> </span>for the ensuing year; that of the Assistant at <sup>$</sup>1,500; that<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Secretary at <sup>$</sup>800., and that he be allowed the use<span class='line-break'> </span>of the office without payment of rent therefor; and that<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Superintendent at <sup>$</sup>2,500., and that the last-named<span class='line-break'> </span>shall have the use of a House and the grounds thereto<span class='line-break'> </span>belonging, the use of a Horse and Vehicle and the services<span class='line-break'> </span>of one Man, at the expense of the Corporation.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills.'><u>Monthly Bills.</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of February 10., showing a total of <sup>$</sup>3,355.18<span class='line-break'> </span>was presented, and it was Voted, that upon approval by<span class='line-break'> </span>the President, payment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives appointed.'><u>Representatives appointed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That Representatives be designated for Lots, as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows:</p>
<p><sup>#</sup>3569. Mary A. Kimball, of Wellesley. Dau.<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>#</sup>4996. William A. Hayes 2nd. of Cambridge Son.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Standing Committees.'><u>Standing Committees.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced the Standing Committees for<span class='line-break'> </span>1897-1898, as follows: -</p>

<p>198</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1897'>1897</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='October 13 No Quorum.'><u>October 13 No Quorum.</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1897-10-13'>October 13, 1897.</date></u></p>
<p>The Monthly Meeting was notified to be held on<span class='line-break'> </span>Wednesday, October 13, 1897, at 2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p><u>No quorum was present.</u></p>
<p>L.G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='October 19 Special Meeting'><u>October 19 Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1897-10-19'>October 19, 1897.</date></u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held as notified on Tuesday, October 19, 1897, at 12:15<span class='line-break'> </span>o'clock P.M.</p>
<p>Present, The President and Messrs. Browne, Cheever,<span class='line-break'> </span>Choate, Eaton, Foster, Johnson, Jones, Sawyer and Shaw.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of May 6, and subse<span class='line-break'></span>quent meetings were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills.'><u>Monthly Bills.</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved the following Schedules of Monthly Bills: -</p>
<p>May 12, 1897, <sup>$</sup>6,510.77; June 9, <sup>$</sup>6,992.23; July 14, <sup>$</sup>6,372.96;<span class='line-break'> </span>August 11, <sup>$</sup>5,338.31; September 8, <sup>$</sup>5,562.68; and that<span class='line-break'> </span>payment of the same had been thereupon made by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer.</p>
<p>Voted, that the action of the President in this<span class='line-break'> </span>regard be fully ratified and approved.</p>
<p>The Schedule of October 13 was presented, showing a<span class='line-break'> </span>total of <sup>$</sup>6991.20, and it was</p>
<p>Voted, that upon approval by the President, pay<span class='line-break'></span>ment thereof be made by the Treasurer.</p>

<p>204</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Rice Lots'><u>Rice Lots</u></span></p>
<p>proprietor of Lot No. 668, that by mistake the inter<span class='line-break'></span>ments of his descendants had been made in the adjoining<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot No. 667, originally owned by Henry Rice deceased,<span class='line-break'> </span>while the interments of his descendants had been made<span class='line-break'> </span>in said Lot No. 668, the matter of making an exchange<span class='line-break'> </span>of the numbers of said Lots, or of transferring the title<span class='line-break'> </span>thereto the respective heirs-at-law or divisees of each<span class='line-break'> </span>of said original proprietors so that said interments shall<span class='line-break'> </span>appear to have been made in the proper Lots, was re<span class='line-break'></span>ferred to the Committee on Lots.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Taking of Land of Cemetery Mt Auburn St.'><u>Taking of Land of Cemetery Mt Auburn St.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That all matters relating to the proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>taking of land of the Corporation fo rthe purpose of<span class='line-break'> </span>widening Mount Auburn Street, either by the City of<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge or the Town of Watertown, be referred to<span class='line-break'> </span>the President with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Bulfinch Pl. Mort. to be Sold.'><u>Bulfinch Pl. Mort. to be Sold.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That the Finance Committee be directed<span class='line-break'> </span>to sell the mortgage now held by the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the Hotel Rexford property on Bulfinch<span class='line-break'> </span>Place, if the same can be done without serious loss.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Notice of Appropriation for Furniture for New Chapel'><u>Notice of Appropriation for Furniture for New Chapel</u></span></p>
<p>The President gave notice that at the next meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing of the Board he should ask for an appropria<span class='line-break'></span>tion of Five Thousand dollars for the purpose of<span class='line-break'> </span>fitting up and furnishing the New Chapel and pro<span class='line-break'></span>viding for the necessary drainage and grading of the<span class='line-break'> </span>grounds surrounding the same.</p>
<p>Dissolved.<span class='line-break'> </span>L.G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>

<p>Jerome Jones.<span class='line-break'> </span>Justice of the peace.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 15. Special Meeting'><u>February 15. Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1898-02-15'>February 15, 1898.</date></u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held, as notified, on Tuesday, February 15, 1898, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:20 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Browne, Choate,<span class='line-break'> </span>Foster, Johnson, Jones, Sawyer and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records read'><u>Records read</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of January 26, 1898, were<span class='line-break'> </span>read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 7, 1898'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 7, 1898</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual Meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing of the Proprietors held on February 7, 1898, Messrs.<span class='line-break'> </span>Israel M. Spelman and Jerome Jones, were chosen as<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to serve for six years, ending 1904.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President.'><u>Election of President.</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a<span class='line-break'> </span>President, it appeared that the whole number of<span class='line-break'> </span>ballots cast was seven, all of which were for Israel<span class='line-break'> </span>M. Spelman, and he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer, Secretary and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer, Secretary and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for a Treasurer, seven,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for H.B. Mackintosh; for a Sec<span class='line-break'></span>retary, seven, all of which were for, L.G. Farmer; and<span class='line-break'> </span>for a Superintendent, seven, all of which were for</p>

<p>James C. Scorgie; and they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.'><u>Salaries fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at <sup>$</sup>2500<span class='line-break'> </span>for the ensuing year; that of the Assistant at <sup>$</sup>1500;<span class='line-break'> </span>that of the Secretary at <sup>$</sup>800, and that he be allowed<span class='line-break'> </span>the use of the office without payment of rent therefor;<span class='line-break'> </span>and that of the Superintendent at <sup>$</sup>2500, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>last-named shall have the use of a House and the<span class='line-break'> </span>grounds thereto belonging, the use of a Horse and<span class='line-break'> </span>Vehicle and the services of one Man, at the expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committees continued'><u>Committees continued</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that all Committees having unfinished busi<span class='line-break'></span>ness in their hands be continued in office, with the same<span class='line-break'> </span>powers as originally conferred upon them.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported that he had examined and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved the Schedule of Monthly Bills for February<span class='line-break'> </span>9, amounting to <sup>$</sup>3310.14, and that payment thereof had<span class='line-break'> </span>been thereupon made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p>Voted, that the action of the President in this re<span class='line-break'></span>gard be fully ratified and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contracts Perpetual Care'><u>Contracts Perpetual Care</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Lots reported the following con<span class='line-break'></span>tracts for perpetual care, all of which were approved<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Board:</p>
<p><sup>#</sup>3. *William Rollins by Heirs <sup>$</sup>375.<span class='line-break'> </span>151. *Julia B.H. James " Executors 1850.<span class='line-break'> </span>1216. *Richard B. Carter " Exr's. of *John W. Carter 400.</p>

<p>first presenting the application for such loan to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board of Trustees for their approval," and substituting<span class='line-break'> </span>therefor the words "without first presenting the applica<span class='line-break'></span>tion for such loan to the Advisory Committee on Loans <span class='line-break'> </span>for their approval"; so that said vote shall read as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows: "Voted, that the Finance Committee be directed<span class='line-break'> </span>to make no larger loan on any note secured by mortgage<span class='line-break'> </span>than a sum equal to one-twentieth of the amount of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Repair Fund, being about Fifty Thousand dollars,<span class='line-break'> </span>without first presenting the application for such loan<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Advisory Committee on Loans, for their approval,<span class='line-break'> </span>the approval of either member of said Committee to be sufficient.</p>

<p>Voted, that the prayer of the petition be granted, upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the condition that the petitioner and his wife be both in<span class='line-break'></span>terred in the same grave space.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Chapel and Office Building Cost of. Architect&apos;s Bill paid.'><u>New Chapel and Office Building Cost of. Architect's Bill paid.</u></span></p>
<p>The President on behalf of the Building Committee,<span class='line-break'> </span>reported the final completion of the New Chapel<span class='line-break'> </span>and Office Building, at a total cost of about <sup>$</sup>68,000,<span class='line-break'> </span>as shown on the Treasurer's books, and that the bill<span class='line-break'> </span>of Mr. W.T. Sears, the achitect, dated November 25th,<span class='line-break'> </span>1898, and amounting to <sup>$</sup>3133.66, or five percent com<span class='line-break'></span>mission on <sup>$</sup>62,673.31, being the amount of expenditrues<span class='line-break'> </span>made under his direction, had been paid. The Pres<span class='line-break'></span>ident stated also that the additional expenditures</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Additional Expenditures on'><u>Additional Expenditures on</u></span></p>
<p>made under the direction of the Building Committee,<span class='line-break'> </span>and which made up the amount of <sup>$</sup>68,000, were for<span class='line-break'> </span>labor on cellar and drains, electrical work and</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137442">
<h3><a name="page-1137442">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 221)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>221</p>
<p>apparatus, hardware, furniture and other articles neces<span class='line-break'></span>sary for the completion and furnishing of the building, in<span class='line-break'></span>cluding also the charges of the three competing architects<span class='line-break'> </span>for their plans.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='First used for Funerals June 18.'><u>First used for Funerals June 18.</u></span></p>
<p>The President also reported that the Chapel, al<span class='line-break'></span>though hardly then completed, was first used for<span class='line-break'> </span>funderals on the 18th. of June; that the last pay<span class='line-break'></span>ment on the Culbert contract was on July 6th; and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the new offices were moved into on July 8th.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committee on Lots to have charge.'><u>Committee on Lots to have charge.</u></span></p>
<p>The President also presented the importance of plac<span class='line-break'></span>ing the Chapel and Office Building under the care of<span class='line-break'> </span>a Committee who should be empowered to make neces<span class='line-break'></span>sary repairs, regulations and charges for the use of the <span class='line-break'> </span>same, receive applications for leave to place Memori<span class='line-break'></span>al Windows therein, and have general charge of all<span class='line-break'> </span>matters pertaining to the building; and upon motion<span class='line-break'> </span>it was Voted, That the Chapel and Office Building<span class='line-break'> </span>be placed under the charge of the Committee on Lots, with<span class='line-break'> </span>full powers.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Claim of Parry Bros. &amp; Co.'><u>Claim of Parry Bros. &amp; Co.</u></span></p>
<p>A letter^377a^was read from the firm of Parry Brothers &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Company, detailing the losses which they had sus<span class='line-break'></span>tained in attempting to carry out the contract of R.J.<span class='line-break'> </span>Culbert for building the New Chapel and Office Building<span class='line-break'> </span>and requesting an allowance from the Corporation to<span class='line-break'> </span>compensate them for such losses, and upon motion,<span class='line-break'> </span>Voted, That the letter be referred to the architect,<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. Sears, with the request that he submit to the Board</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #4072 Request of Eliza J. Chamberlin to erect Monument.'><u>Lot <sup>#</sup>4072 Request of Eliza J. Chamberlin to erect Monument.</u></span></p>
<p>An application^378^was received from Mrs. Eliza J. Cham<span class='line-break'></span>berlin, widow of Lowell W. Chamberlin, late proprietor of<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot No. 4072 for permission to remove two Headstones<span class='line-break'> </span>therefrom and to erect a granite Monument thereon.<span class='line-break'> </span>As it appeared that the sum of <sup>$</sup>500 had been paid<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Corporation as a donation in trust for the care of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Lot and that by the will of the late proprietor<span class='line-break'> </span>the same had been devised to the Corporation in trust<span class='line-break'> </span>to be kept as a burial place for himself and the said<span class='line-break'> </span>Eliza J. Chamberlin and no others, it was</p>
<p>Voted that leave be granted as prayed for, sub<span class='line-break'></span>ject to the approval of the President, and upon the<span class='line-break'> </span>conditions that the Headstones now on the Lot be not<span class='line-break'> </span>removed, or buried in the ground, and that the graves<span class='line-break'> </span>in the Lot be not disturbed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Crematory at Cemetery'><u>Crematory at Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>The President made a statement to the Board in<span class='line-break'> </span>regard to the establishment of a Crematory at the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery to the effect that the surveys he had had<span class='line-break'> </span>made showed that there was ample room for a<span class='line-break'> </span>Crematory on the North side of the old Chapel, and that<span class='line-break'> </span>he had every reason for believing that such location would<span class='line-break'> </span>be approved by the Board of Health. He stated fur<span class='line-break'></span>ther that the Superintendent had visited the crematories<span class='line-break'> </span>at Brooklyn, Philadelphia and Troy and called upon<span class='line-break'> </span>him to give the results of his examination into the<span class='line-break'> </span>matter. After hearing the statements of the Super-</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Crematory at Cemetery'><u>Crematory at Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>the meeting of December 16, 1898.    After some dis<span class='line-break'></span>cussion it appeared to be the opinion of the Board<span class='line-break'> </span>that is was not within their power to authorize the ex<span class='line-break'></span>penditure of the money of the Corporation for such a<span class='line-break'> </span>purpose, and it was accordingly voted<span class='line-break'> </span>That the petitioners have leave to withdraw.<span class='line-break'> </span>The President, to whom was referred the subject of the <span class='line-break'> </span>establishment of a Crematory at the Cemetery, reported<span class='line-break'> </span>that he had given the subject due consideration <span class='line-break'> </span>and presented the following vote which was passed.<span class='line-break'> </span>Voted, That the President be authorized to employ<span class='line-break'> </span>an architect and have plans and estimates made<span class='line-break'> </span>for the construction of a Crematory on the north side<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Old Chapel, and for such alterations and im<span class='line-break'></span>provements in the Old Chapel as may be necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>to connect it with the Crematory.<span class='line-break'> </span>Dissolved.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Standing Committees'><u>Standing Committees</u></span></p>
<p>The President then announced the Standing Committees<span class='line-break'> </span>for 1899-1900, as follows:</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Grounds'><u>Grounds</u></span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lots'><u>Lots</u></span></p>

<p><u>Advisory Committee on Loans</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Whitney and Johnson.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committees Continued'><u>Committees Continued</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That all Committees having unfinished business<span class='line-break'> </span>in their hands be continued in office, with the same<span class='line-break'> </span>powers as originally conferred upon them.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Crematory Notice of Appropriation'><u>Crematory Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported informally to the Board the<span class='line-break'> </span>progress which had been made in the matter of the<span class='line-break'> </span>establishment of a Crematory at the Cemetery, and<span class='line-break'> </span>gave notice that at the next meeting of the Board<span class='line-break'> </span>he should ask for an appropriation not exceeding<span class='line-break'> </span>Fifteen Thousand dollars to be expended in the erect<span class='line-break'></span>ion of a Crematory building.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Greenhouses Notice of Appropriation'><u>Greenhouses Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President also gave notice that at the next meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board he should ask for an appropriation not exceed<span class='line-break'></span>ing Three Thousand dollars to be expended in necessary re<span class='line-break'></span>pairs to the Greenhouses at the Cemetery. Dissolved</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137454">
<h3><a name="page-1137454">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 233)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>233</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Greenhouses Appropriation Voted'><u>Greenhouses Appropriation Voted</u></span></p>
<p>The President, in accordance with the notice given at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of <date when='1899-02-20'>February 20, 1899,</date> asked for an appropriation of<span class='line-break'> </span>Three Thousand dollars to be expended in necessary repairs<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Greenhouses at the Cemetery, and it was</p>
<p>Voted, That the sum of Three Thousand dollars be ap<span class='line-break'></span>propriated for that purpose.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Crematory Appropriation Voted.'><u>Crematory Appropriation Voted.</u></span></p>
<p>The President, in accordance with the notice given at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of <date when='1899-02-20'>February 20, 1899,</date> asked for an appropriation of<span class='line-break'> </span>Fifteen Thousand dollars, to be expended in the erection<span class='line-break'> </span>of a Crematory building at the Cemetery, and it was</p>
<p>Voted, That the sum of Fifteen Thousand dollars be<span class='line-break'> </span>appropriated for that purpose.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Plans approved'><u>Plans approved</u></span></p>
<p>Mr. Willard T. Sears then presented plans showing pro<span class='line-break'></span>posed alterations in the Old Chapel to render it available for the<span class='line-break'> </span>purposes of a Crematory, and explained the same to the Board,<span class='line-break'> </span>in detail. After extended general discussion, it was</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Vote'><u>Vote</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That the plan of altering the Old Chapel for use as a<span class='line-break'> </span>Crematory be adopted, and that the President be, and he here<span class='line-break'></span>by is, instructed and empowered to first obtain the appro<span class='line-break'></span>val of the State Board of Health, and then to make all neces<span class='line-break'></span>sary contracts for the alteration of the Old Chapel into a<span class='line-break'> </span>Crematory substantially in accordance with the plans presented<span class='line-break'> </span>by Mr. Sears.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Telephone at Office'><u>Telephone at Office</u></span></p>
<p>The subject of placing a telephone in the office at Boston<span class='line-break'> </span>was presented and, after discussion, it was Voted, that the<span class='line-break'> </span>matter be left in the hands of the President, with power.</p>
<p>Dissolved. L.G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Resolutions on death of Samuel Johnson'><u>Resolutions on death of Samuel Johnson</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That we wish to enter on our records our high<span class='line-break'> </span>appreciation of our late associate, Samuel Johnson. Upon<span class='line-break'> </span>his judgment and ability we could always rely,<span class='line-break'> </span>and his long financial experience and business<span class='line-break'> </span>capacity eminently fitted him to perform the duties<span class='line-break'> </span>of a Trustee. We feel also that by his death<span class='line-break'> </span>we have lost a true friend whose courteous manners<span class='line-break'> </span>and cheerful, buoyant temper endeared him to all.</p>
<p>Voted. That the Secretary be directed to send a copy of<span class='line-break'> </span>these votes to the family and relatives of our lamented friend</p>

<div id="page-1137462">
<h3><a name="page-1137462">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 241)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>241</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Rate of Interest for Perpetual Repair Contracts fixed.'><u>Rate of Interest for Perpetual Repair Contracts fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>The President, for the Committee on Lots, presented the<span class='line-break'> </span>following votes which were passed:</p>
<p>Voted. That the rate of interest by which the amount of<span class='line-break'> </span>principal required to meet the annual charge for ex<span class='line-break'></span>penses is ascertained in applications for perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of lots be fixed at three percent to all new<span class='line-break'> </span>applicants from and after this date, instead of four<span class='line-break'> </span>percent as heretofore charged.</p>
<p>Voted. That the Treasurer shall not hold as in force<span class='line-break'> </span>any estimates already made by the Superintendent and<span class='line-break'> </span>send out to applicants for the same after three months<span class='line-break'> </span>from the date of said estimates.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Examina-tion of Mortgages'><u>Examina-tion of Mortgages</u></span></p>
<p>Voted. That the President be directed to have the<span class='line-break'> </span>notes and mortgages in which the funds of this corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration are mostly invested, carefully examined in re<span class='line-break'></span>gard to their security and values, and for this pur<span class='line-break'></span>pose he be authorized to employ competent legal<span class='line-break'> </span>counsel and real estate experts, the results of their<span class='line-break'> </span>examination to be reported to this Board.</p>
<p>Dissolved.</p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
</div>

<p>bers being detained by illness and business engage<span class='line-break'></span>ments, no quorum was present. The following<span class='line-break'> </span>paper approving the Annual Report of the Trustees</p>

<p>(Copy)</p>
<p>"We, the undersigned, Trustees, have read and<span class='line-break'> </span>approved of the sixty-eighth Annual<sup>386</sup> Report of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>together with the Reports<sup>387</sup> of the Treasurer and<sup>388</sup> Superin<span class='line-break'></span>tendent signed by the President for the Trustees, and<span class='line-break'> </span>authorize the same to be issued and sent to the Propri<span class='line-break'></span>etors in accordance with vote usually issued at the meet<span class='line-break'></span>ing called for that purpose." [Signed]</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President.'><u>Election of President.</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a President,<span class='line-break'> </span>it appeared that the whole number of ballots cast was<span class='line-break'> </span>seven all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he<span class='line-break'> </span>was declared elected.</p>

<p>252<span class='line-break'> </span>[Cremation]  Old Chapel had been completed and that it was in <span class='line-break'> </span>[begun] satisfactory use for the incinerattion of bodies the <span class='line-break'> </span>approved of the State Board of Health having been <span class='line-break'> </span>received on April 7 last. <p>===<u>Coolidge Ave. Sale of "Stone Meadow" authorized</u></p>
<p>The Committee of Conference appointed at the meet<span class='line-break'></span>tine of October 12, reported that they had conferred <span class='line-break'> </span>with the Committee of the Board of Cemetery Com<span class='line-break'></span>missioners of the C ity of Cambridge in regard to the <span class='line-break'> </span>proposed acquisition by the city of certain land of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation on Coolidge Avenue, and it was Voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>That, in the judgment of the Board of Trustees, the</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137485">
<h3><a name="page-1137485">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 263)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>263</p>
<p>"Stone Meadow, so called, be sold for not less than<span class='line-break'> </span>Thirty-two thousand dollars, but that power be given to <span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee to negotiate such sale with the Committee <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board of Cemebery Commissioners of the City of Cam<span class='line-break'></span>bridge at a price not less than Thirty thousand dol<span class='line-break'></span>lars, possession not to be given until the expiration of <span class='line-break'> </span>one year from the date of the deed, and the right to be <span class='line-break'> </span>re[?]ved to the Corporation to drain through the water<span class='line-break'></span>course in said land, as at present existing.</p>
<p>===<u>Repair Fulnd Proposed Amendment to </u></p>
<p>The Finance Committee having represented to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Board the great difficulty experienced by them in <span class='line-break'> </span>procuring suitable mortgages for the investment of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Repair Fund, making it desirable that some action <span class='line-break'> </span>be taken by the Corporation whereby the scope of in<span class='line-break'></span>vestments may be materially enlarged, it was Voted,</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Article VIII. By-Laws'><u>Article VIII. By-Laws</u></span></p>
<p>That a Committee of four be appointed by the <span class='line-break'> </span>President, to consider the subject of making such <span class='line-break'> </span>changes in Article VIII of the By-Laws as will enlarge <span class='line-break'> </span>the field of investments now permitted for the Repair Fund<span class='line-break'> </span>and report their conclusions at the next meeting of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board, in order that the same may be emobodied in an <span class='line-break'> </span>amendment to said Article VIII, to be acted upon at the <span class='line-break'> </span>next annual meeting.</p>
<p>The President appointed Messrs. Choate, Whitney, Watson <span class='line-break'> </span>and Cummings as such Committee, upon motion the <span class='line-break'> </span>President was added thereto.   <u>Dissolved</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer, Secretary</p>

<p>The records of the special meeting of November 26.<span class='line-break'> </span>were read and approved</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contract Perpetual Care'><u>Contract Perpetual Care</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Lots recommended a contract <span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual care of Lot #3904 with the heirs of <span class='line-break'> </span>Caleb William Loring, the late proprietor, and the same <span class='line-break'> </span>was approved by the Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives appointed'><u>Representatives appointed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that Mary A. Richards, of Cambridge, the <span class='line-break'> </span>widow of the lastye proprietor be designated as Represent<span class='line-break'></span>ative of Lot #4235.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The President reported, that he had examined <span class='line-break'> </span>and approved the Schedule of Monthly Bills for Decem<span class='line-break'></span>ber 12, 1900, amounting to $3946.52, and that the same had <span class='line-break'> </span>been thereupon paid by the Treasurer, and it was  Voted,<span class='line-break'> </span>that the action of the President in this regard be fully <span class='line-break'> </span>ratified and approved.</p>

<div id="page-1137509">
<h3><a name="page-1137509">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 275)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>275</p>
<p>Article VI of the By Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Sale of Bradford Estate Voted'><u>Sale of Bradford Estate Voted</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That the Finance Committee be authorized to<span class='line-break'> </span>sell the Lots numbered ONe hundred and six (106) and<span class='line-break'> </span>One hundred and seven (107) on plan of the Bradford<span class='line-break'> </span>Estate on South Street, West Roxbury, district of Boston,<span class='line-break'> </span>made by Charles H.W. Wood, dated <date when='1896-06-01'>June 1, 1896</date>, acquired<span class='line-break'> </span>by foreclosure of mortgage, on such terms as they shall<span class='line-break'> </span>see fit; and that the Treasurer be authorized to exe<span class='line-break'></span>cute and deliver quitclaim deed of said estate ap<span class='line-break'></span>proved by the Finance Committee.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='New Greenhouse Appropriation Voted'><u>New Greenhouse Appropriation Voted</u></span></p>
<p>The President, in accordance with the notice given at the<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting of February 14, last, asked for an appropriation<span class='line-break'> </span>of Four Thousand dollars (<sup>$</sup>4000.), to be expended in the<span class='line-break'> </span>erection of a new Greenhouse at the Cemetery, and it was</p>
<p>Voted, that the sum of Four Thousand dollars (<sup>$</sup>4000) be<span class='line-break'> </span>appropriated for this purpose, and that such Green<span class='line-break'></span>house be built under the direction of the President.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Memorial Service to Governor Wolcott'><u>Memorial Service to Governor Wolcott</u></span></p>
<p>A letter of invitation, with tickets enclosed,<span class='line-break'> </span>from the Committee of Arrangements for the public<span class='line-break'> </span>service in memory of the late Governor Roger Wolcott,<span class='line-break'> </span>formerly a member of the Board of Trustees, was<span class='line-break'> </span>presented, and it was Voted, that the invitation<span class='line-break'> </span>be accepted with thanks, and that the President<span class='line-break'> </span>be given discretionary power to appoint a committee<span class='line-break'> </span>to attend the service on Thursday, April 18.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Resolutions on death of Joseph Sawyer.'><u>Resolutions on death of Joseph Sawyer.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, That we wish to enter on our Records our ap<span class='line-break'></span>preciation of the services of Joseph Sawyer, lately a<span class='line-break'> </span>member of this Board. Chosen in 1893 to fill the vacancy<span class='line-break'> </span>caused by the resignation of the late Samuel R. Payson,<span class='line-break'> </span>he continued to serve by re-election until the oc<span class='line-break'></span>currence of his death on the twenty-seventh day of<span class='line-break'> </span>May last.</p>
<p>As a Trustee he was always ready to give us the<span class='line-break'> </span>benefit of his judgment and experience, and faith<span class='line-break'></span>fully performed all the duties which devolved upon<span class='line-break'> </span>him.</p>
<p>Voted, That the Secretary send a copy of this vote to <span class='line-break'> </span>the members of his family.</p>
