<div id="page-1137523">
<h3><a name="page-1137523">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 282)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>282</p>
<p>===<u>Annual Reports.</u></p>
<p>The President having presented and read the Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Report<sup>401</sup> to the Proprietors, it was Voted,</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='President.'><u>President.</u></span></p>
<p>That the same be approved and adopted as the Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Report of the Trustees to the Proprietors and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>same be printed and distributed to them accordingly.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>The Report<sup>402</sup> of the Treasurer, as approved by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Finance, and that<sup>403</sup> of the Superintend<span class='line-break'></span>ent having also been presented, it was Voted,</p>
<p>That the same be accepted, printed and distributed<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Proprietors.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #1027 Petition of Heirs of *Eliza Brown'><u>Lot <sup>#</sup>1027 Petition of Heirs of *Eliza Brown</u></span></p>
<p>A petition<sup>404</sup> was presented from the Heirs of the<span class='line-break'> </span>late Eliza Brown, proprietor of Lot No. 1027, for<span class='line-break'> </span>a re-location of said Lot, according to a plan thereof<span class='line-break'> </span>annexed to said petition, and it was Voted,</p>
<p>That the subject be referred to the Committee on Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>with power.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contribution to City of Cambridge for Street Watering'><u>Contribution to City of Cambridge for Street Watering</u></span></p>
<p>The President read a communication from the Treas<span class='line-break'></span>urer of the City of Cambridge, soliciting a contribution<span class='line-break'> </span>from the Corporation towards the expense of watering<span class='line-break'> </span>the streets in the vicinity of the Cemetery for the years, 1899,<span class='line-break'> </span>1900 and 1901, and, after discussion, it was Voted,</p>
<p>That the Treasurer pay to the City of Cambridge the sum<span class='line-break'> </span>of One Hundred and Eighty dollars as a voluntary con<span class='line-break'></span>tribution towards the expense of watering the streets in<span class='line-break'> </span>the vicinity of the Cemetery for the years, 1899, 1900 and 1901,<span class='line-break'> </span>provided the City Treasurer sign a receipt for the same,<span class='line-break'> </span>showing it to be a voluntary contribution.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137525">
<h3><a name="page-1137525">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 283)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>283</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Request of M.A. Yardley'><u>Request of M.A. Yardley</u></span></p>
<p>The President read a letter<sup>405</sup> from Miss M.A. Yard<span class='line-break'></span>ley, of Boston, asking permission to place on the wall<span class='line-break'> </span>of the New Chapel a memorial tablet to Mary Yardley,<span class='line-break'> </span>now buried in Dr. Bowditch's lot, and it was Voted,</p>
<p>inexpedient to grant this request.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Place of Annual Meeting'><u>Place of Annual Meeting</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the Annual Meeting of the Proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>be held on the first Monday of February next at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 o'clock in the afternoon, at the office of the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration, No. 5 Tremont Street, Boston.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Revision of By-Laws'><u>Revision of By-Laws</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that a committee of two be appointed to<span class='line-break'> </span>consider the subject of changes in the By-Laws<span class='line-break'> </span>and Regulations of the Corporation or in the statutes<span class='line-break'> </span>relating thereto, and report at the next meeting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Board, and the President appointed Messrs.<span class='line-break'> </span>Hutchins and Watson as such committee.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secretary&apos;s Oath'><u>Secretary's Oath</u></span></p>
<p>Commonwealth of Massachusetts.<span class='line-break'> </span>Suffolk, ss. Boston, A.D. 1902.</p>
<p>Personally appeared Lewis G. Farmer and made<span class='line-break'> </span>oath that he would faithfully and impartially discharge<span class='line-break'> </span>the duties of Secretary of the Proprietors of the Cemetery of<span class='line-break'> </span>Mount Auburn, before me</p>
<p>justice of the peace.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1137527">
<h3><a name="page-1137527">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 284)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>284</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='1902'>1902</span></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 12 Special Meeting'><u>February 12 Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1902-02-12'>February 12, 1902</date></u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held, as notified, on Wednesday, February 12, 1902, at<span class='line-break'> </span>2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Beal, Cheever,<span class='line-break'> </span>Choate, Cummings, Foster, Hutchins, Reynolds and<span class='line-break'> </span>Watson.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of January 10, 1902 were<span class='line-break'> </span>read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected Feb. 3, 1902'><u>Trustees elected Feb. 3, 1902</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting of the Proprietors, held on <date when='1902-02-03'>February 3, 1902</date>,<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Charles F. Choate and Joshua M. Sears<span class='line-break'> </span>were chosen as Trustees, to serve for six years,<span class='line-break'> </span>ending 1908 and that Mr. Thomas P. Beal was<span class='line-break'> </span>chosen a Trustee to serve until 1907, to fill the va<span class='line-break'></span>cancy caused by the death of Mr. Joseph Sawyer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a<span class='line-break'> </span>President, it appeared that the whole number of<span class='line-break'> </span>ballots cast was seven, all of which were for Israel<span class='line-break'> </span>M. Spelman, and he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer Assistant Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer Assistant Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for the election of a<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer, eight, all of which were for John L. Dill;<span class='line-break'> </span>for an Assistant Treasurer, eight, all of which were<span class='line-break'> </span>for Henry B. Mackintosh; for a Secretary, eight, all<span class='line-break'> </span>of which were for Lewis G. Farmer; and for a Su<span class='line-break'></span>perintendent, eight, all of which were for James C.<span class='line-break'> </span>Scorgie, and they were severally declared elected.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137529">
<h3><a name="page-1137529">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 285)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>285</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed'><u>Salaries fixed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at<span class='line-break'> </span>Twenty seven Hundred and Fifty dollars fo rthe en<span class='line-break'></span>suing year; that of the Assistant Treasurer at Fifteen<span class='line-break'> </span>Hundred dollars; that of the Secretary at Eight Hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars, and that he be allowed the use of the office<span class='line-break'> </span>without payment of rent therefor; and that of the Su<span class='line-break'></span>perintendent at Three Thousand dollars, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>last-named shall have the use of a House and the<span class='line-break'> </span>grounds thereto belonging, the use of a Horse and Vehicle<span class='line-break'> </span>and the services of one Man, at the expense of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation.</p>
<p>Voted, also, that Albert C. Dean be employed as a <span class='line-break'> </span>Clerk, at a salary of Fifteen Hundred dollars.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills for February 12, was<span class='line-break'> </span>presented, showing a total of <sup>$</sup>5129.91, and it was voted<span class='line-break'> </span>that upon approval by the President payment thereof<span class='line-break'> </span>be made by the Treasurer.</p>

Farmer, the executor of said will <span class='line-break'> </span>has presented for allowance in said Probate Court <span class='line-break'> </span>his first and final acount as such executor, and it<span class='line-break'> </span>appears therefore that the residue of said estate in his <span class='line-break'> </span>hands amounts, in cash and securities, to the sum of <span class='line-break'> </span>Sixteen Thousand Three Hundred and Thirty-eight &amp; 9/100<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars, which he desires to pay over to said Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>in fulfilment of the provision of said will in that behalf:<span class='line-break'> </span>it is, therefore, voted that said bequest abe accepted by <span class='line-break'> </span>said Corporation for the uses and purposes said will<span class='line-break'> </span>set forth, and that the Treasurer be, and he hereby is,<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized and empowered in the name and on behalf of <span class='line-break'> </span>said Corporation, to assent to the allowance of said account<span class='line-break'> </span>and to give to the said Lewis G. <p>313</p>
<p>the date of such notice, the Superintendent put them in<span class='line-break'> </span>proper order, under the direction of the President, at the ex<span class='line-break'></span>pense of the respective Proprietors, as provided by Article VI<span class='line-break'> </span>of the By-Laws.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Steam Roller &amp;c. Notice of Appropriation'><u>Steam Roller &amp;c. Notice of Appropriation</u></span></p>
<p>The President gave notice that at the next meeting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Board, he should ask for an appropriation not exceed<span class='line-break'></span>ing Nine Thousand dollars, to be expended in the purchase<span class='line-break'> </span>of a new Steam Roller, Crusher, Engine and Dynamo,<span class='line-break'> </span>and in the erection of a House and digging of a Cellar.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='R.W. Shapleigh Request #4297'><u>R.W. Shapleigh Request #4297</u></span></p>
<p>A request<sup>422</sup> was received from Mr. J.R.W. Shapleigh that he be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed to place a granite field Boulder, temporarily on<span class='line-break'> </span>land of the Corporation adjoining Lot No. 4297, with the in<span class='line-break'></span>tention of placing the same at a later period ove rthe<span class='line-break'> </span>graves of himself and wife in said Lot as a Monument;<span class='line-break'> </span>and it was voted that his request be granted, provided<span class='line-break'> </span>that he make a satisfactory contract to pay all the cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of moving and placing the same and of its removal, if the<span class='line-break'> </span>same should be ordered by the Board, and also to comply<span class='line-break'> </span>with such an order, if made.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Street Watering Contribution to City of Cambridge.'><u>Street Watering Contribution to City of Cambridge.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Treasurer pay to the City of Cam<span class='line-break'></span>bridge the sum of Sixty dollars as a voluntary contribu<span class='line-break'></span>tion towards the expense of watering the streets in the vi<span class='line-break'></span>cinity of the Cemetery for the year 1903, provided that the<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer of said City sign a receipt for the same, showing<span class='line-break'> </span>it to be a voluntary contribution.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved</u></p>
<p>Lewis G. Farmer, Secretary.</p>

<p>Voted that the Treasurer be, and he hereby is, author<span class='line-break'></span>ized and directed to sign, seal with the corporate seal<span class='line-break'> </span>and deliver as the act of the Corporation, a deed of Lot No.<span class='line-break'> </span>5878, to one Charles F. <p><date when='1904-01-13'>January 13, 1904.</date></p>

<p>No quorum was present.</p>

<div id="page-1137654">
<h3><a name="page-1137654">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 317)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>317</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='February 5 Special Meeting'><u>February 5 Special Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><u><date when='1904-02-05'>February 5, 1904.</date></u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was held,<span class='line-break'> </span>as notified, on Friday, February 5, 1904, at 2:30 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Cheever, Choate,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cummings, Foster, Hutchins, Reynolds, Sears and Watson.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the Special Meeting of January 8 were read<span class='line-break'> </span>and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected February 1, 1904.'><u>Trustees elected February 1, 1904.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Proprietors held on <date when='1904-02-01'>February 1, 1904,</date> Messrs Israel<span class='line-break'> </span>M. Spelman and Edward W. Hutchins were re-elected as<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees to serve for six years, ending 1910.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a President,<span class='line-break'> </span>it appeared that the whole number of ballots cast was<span class='line-break'> </span>eight, all of which were for Israel M. Spelman, and he<span class='line-break'> </span>was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent.'><u>Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent.</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for the election of a Treasurer,<span class='line-break'> </span>nine, all of which were for John L. Dill; for a Secretary, nine,<span class='line-break'> </span>all of which were for Lewis G. Farmer; and for a Superintendent,<span class='line-break'> </span>nine, all of which were for James C. Scorgie, and they were<span class='line-break'> </span>severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed'><u>Salaries fixed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at Three<span class='line-break'> </span>Thousand dollars for the ensuing year; that of the Secretary<span class='line-break'> </span>at One Thousand dollars, and that he be allowed the use of<span class='line-break'> </span>the office without payment of rent therefor; and that of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Superintendent at Three Thousand, Five Hundred dollars,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the last named shall have the use of a House<span class='line-break'> </span>and the grounds thereto belonging, the use of a Horse<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137658">
<h3><a name="page-1137658">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 318)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>318</p>
<p>and Vehicle and the services of one Man, at the expense of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation.</p>
<p>Voted, also, that Albert C. Dean be employed as a Clerk,<span class='line-break'> </span>at a salary of Fifteen Hundred dollars.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Portrait of Mr. Spelman'><u>Portrait of Mr. Spelman</u></span></p>
<p>On motion of Mr. Sears, it was voted that, in recognition of<span class='line-break'> </span>the long and devoted services of Mr. Israel M. Spelman,<span class='line-break'> </span>as President of the Corporation, a Committee of two<span class='line-break'> </span>be appointed to cause a suitable portrait of Mr. Spelman<span class='line-break'> </span>to be painted at the expense of the Corporation, the same<span class='line-break'> </span>to be kept in the Office Building at the Cemetery; and<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Sears and Choate were appointed by the Presi<span class='line-break'></span>dent to act as such Committee.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly Bills'><u>Monthly Bills</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills for February 5 was<span class='line-break'> </span>presented, showing a total of <sup>$</sup>4,296.35; and it was voted<span class='line-break'> </span>that, upon approval by the President, payment thereof<span class='line-break'> </span>be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer to sign Bonds when due.'><u>Treasurer to sign Bonds when due.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the Treasurer, John L. Dill, be, and he hereby<span class='line-break'> </span>is, authorized, with the approval of one of the members of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee on Finance, to sign and transfer any bonds<span class='line-break'> </span>belonging to the Corporation which may, at any time here<span class='line-break'></span>after, become due and payable.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives appointed'><u>Representatives appointed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that Representatives be designated for Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>as follows:<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>#</sup>1890. Samuel H. Ordway. of New York, Grandson<span class='line-break'> </span>4193. Hattie A. Gross. " Somerville Daughter.<span class='line-break'> </span>4605 H.H. Learnard " Newton Grandson<span class='line-break'> </span>5038. William H. Howland " Newton Son.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Annual Reports, President'><u>Annual Reports, President</u></span></p>
<p>The President having presented and read the<sup>433</sup> Annual<span class='line-break'> </span>Report to the Proprietors, it was Voted, that the same<span class='line-break'> </span>be approved and adopted as the Annual Report of<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees to the Proprietors and that it be printed<span class='line-break'> </span>and distributed to them accordingly.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>The Report<sup>434</sup> of the Treasurer, as approved by the Com<span class='line-break'></span>mittee on Finance, and that<sup>435</sup> of the Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>having also been presented, it was Voted, that the same be<span class='line-break'> </span>accepted, printed and distributed to the Proprietors.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Office Furniture &amp;c.'><u>Office Furniture &amp;c.</u></span></p>
<p>Mr. Watson, on behalf of the Committee having in charge<span class='line-break'> </span>the duty of securing office accommodations for the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, reported that they had found it necessary to<span class='line-break'> </span>purchase certain furniture and rugs for the proper<span class='line-break'> </span>fitting up of the offices, and asked that their action<span class='line-break'> </span>in so doing be ratified by the Board. They also<span class='line-break'> </span>recommended the purchase of a typewriter for the use<span class='line-break'> </span>of the office, and it was voted, that the action of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee be approved and that they be authorized to<span class='line-break'> </span>purchase a typewriter for the use of the Corporation.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p><u><date when='1905-02-08'>February 15, 1905</date></u></p>
<p>A Special Meeting of the Board of Trustees was held<span class='line-break'> </span>as notified, on Wednesday, February 15, 1905, at 2 o'clock, P.M.</p>
<p>Present, the President and Messrs. Beal, Choate, Hutchins,<span class='line-break'> </span>Russell, Watson and Whitney.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The records of the meeting of January 11 were read and approved</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees elected February 6, 1905.'><u>Trustees elected February 6, 1905.</u></span></p>
<p>The President announced that at the Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of teh Proprietors held on <date when='1905-02-06'>February 6, 1905,</date> Messrs. Frank<span class='line-break'> </span>W. Reynolds and Joseph B. Russell were re-elected as<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, to serve for six years, ending 1911.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent.'><u>Election of President Treasurer Secretary and Superintendent.</u></span></p>
<p>On motion, it was voted that the ballot for the election<span class='line-break'> </span>of officers for the ensuing year be taken at one and the<span class='line-break'> </span>same time; and a ballot having been taken accordingly,<span class='line-break'> </span>it appeared that the whole number of ballots cast was<span class='line-break'> </span>Seven, all of which were to Israel M. Spelman for<span class='line-break'> </span>President, John L. Dill for Treasurer, Lewis G. Farmer<span class='line-break'> </span>for Secretary and James C. Scorgie for Superintendent;<span class='line-break'> </span>and they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed.'><u>Salaries fixed.</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the salary of the Treasurer be fixed at Three<span class='line-break'> </span>Thousand dollars for the ensuing year; that of the Secretary</p>

<p>Mr. Choate for the Committee appointed to prepare<span class='line-break'> </span>resolutions on the death of the late Joshua M. Sears reported the<span class='line-break'> </span>following <sup>448</sup>:  "The Trustees are desirous of entering upon their<span class='line-break'> </span>records, their deep sorrow at the death of Joshua Montgomery Sears.<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. Sears was elected a Trustee at the Annual Meeting on Feb<span class='line-break'></span>ruary 4, 1881, and continued in the office until his death on <span class='line-break'> </span>June 2, 1905, and served as a member of the Committee on <span class='line-break'> </span>Grounds during the whole time.</p>
<p>Interested in horticulture and landscape gardening and <span class='line-break'> </span>always active and attentive to business and familiar with <span class='line-break'> </span>financial affairs, his services have been of great value to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation.  We have always found him a pleasant associate<span class='line-break'> </span>and reliable friend, and our long connection with him will<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

Spelman] The President having stated to the Board that Mr. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Resignation] Spelman had expressed his unwillingness to withdraw<span class='line-break'> </span>[as Trustee] his resignation as Trustee it was voted that the same <span class='line-break'> </span>[accepted] be accepted. <span class='line-break'> </span>Dr. Cheever on behalf of the Committee appointed to <span class='line-break'> </span>prepare resolutions in recognition of Mr. Spelman's services<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Corporation then presented the following:<span class='line-break'> </span>[Resolutions] "The Trustees desire to put upon record their appreciat<span class='line-break'></span>[adopted] tion of the long and faithful services of their retiring <span class='line-break'> </span>President Mr. Israel Munson Spelman. <span class='line-break'> </span>Taking charge of the Cemetery Trust in 1874 he has gra<span class='line-break'></span>tuitorasly and unwearingly continued as itt presiding<span class='line-break'> </span>officer, and practically its manager, for more than thirty- <span class='line-break'> </span>years Holding this position so long, and during so<span class='line-break'> </span>critical a time, his place in the history of the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>is unique; and it is doubtful if any successor can <span class='line-break'> </span>render services so important as his. During this time<span class='line-break'> </span>he has seen the Cemetery become one of the largest<span class='line-break'> </span>examples of a rural burial place; growing in plan<span class='line-break'></span>tations and in gardens year by year, Similarly the <span class='line-break'> </span>cares and responsibilities of its aggregating capital <span class='line-break'> </span>and business have required and have obtained at his <span class='line-break'> </span>hands, honorable careful and constant supervision. </p>

<p>349<span class='line-break'> </span>[February 14] February 14, 1906<span class='line-break'> </span>[Meeting] The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees was <span class='line-break'> </span>held, as notified, on Wednesday February 14, 1906 at<span class='line-break'> </span>12 o'clock noon. <span class='line-break'> </span>Present, Messrs., Beal, Cheever, Choate, Foster, Hem<span class='line-break'></span>enway, Hobbs, Hurkins, Jones, Russell and Watson. <span class='line-break'> </span>In the absence of the President Mr. Choate was <span class='line-break'> </span>chosen temporary Chairman. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Records] The records of the meeting of January 10 were read<span class='line-break'> </span>and approved. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Trustees] The Chairman announced that at the Annual Meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>[elected] of the Proprietors held on February 5, 1906 Mr. Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span>[Feb. 5, 1906] W. Hobbs was elected as a Trustee to serve until 1908,<span class='line-break'> </span>to complete the term of the late Joshua M. Sears; Jerome<span class='line-break'> </span>Jones, to serve until 1910 to complete the term of Israel <span class='line-break'> </span>M. Spelman, resigned; Alfred Hummenway, to serve until <span class='line-break'> </span>1911 to complete the term of the late Frank W. Reynolds; <span class='line-break'> </span>and Prentis Cummings and Charles N. Watson to <span class='line-break'> </span>serve until 1912. The Chairman also announced<span class='line-break'> </span>that the proposed amendment of Article II of the <span class='line-break'> </span>By-Laws reported at the meeting of January 10, <span class='line-break'> </span>had been submitted to the Proprietors at the Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>Meeting and had been unaninmously adopted.<span class='line-break'> </span>[Frank W.] A letter was read from Robert D. Reynolds a son of the <span class='line-break'> </span>[Reynolds] late Frank W. Reynolds expressing the appreciation of <span class='line-break'> </span>[Letter from Son] his family of the vote adopted at the meeting of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Board, held on January 10. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137781">
<h3><a name="page-1137781">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 350)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>350</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Election of President'><u>Election of President</u></span></p>
<p>A ballot having been taken for the election of a<span class='line-break'> </span>President, it appeared that the whole number of ballots<span class='line-break'> </span>cast was ten, all of which were for Prentiss Cummings, <span class='line-break'> </span>and he was declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer, Secretary and Superintendent'><u>Treasurer, Secretary and Superintendent</u></span></p>
<p>Whole number of ballots cast for the election of a Treas<span class='line-break'></span>urer, ten, all of which were for John L. Dill; for a Secre<span class='line-break'></span>tary, ten, all of which were for Lewis G. Farmer; and for a <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent, ten, all of which were for James C. Scorgie; <span class='line-break'> </span>and they were severally declared elected.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Salaries fixed'><u>Salaries fixed</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Salary of the President be fixed at <span class='line-break'> </span>Three Thousand dollars for the ensuing year, together with<span class='line-break'> </span>the use of the small office adjoining that of the Treasurer, <span class='line-break'> </span>without payment of rent therefor; that of the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>at Three Thousand dollars; that of the Secretary at One<span class='line-break'> </span>Thousand dollars, and that he be allowed the use of the <span class='line-break'> </span>office without payment of rent therefor; and that of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Superintendent at Three Thousand, Five Hundred dollars <span class='line-break'> </span>and that the last named shall have the use of a House<span class='line-break'> </span>and the grounds there to belonging, the use of a Horse <span class='line-break'> </span>and Vehicle, and the service of one Man, at the expense <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation.</p>
<p>Voted, also, that Albert C. Dean be employed as a Clerk <span class='line-break'> </span>at a Salary of Fifteen Hundred dollars.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Time and Hour of Meetings'><u>Time and Hour of Meetings</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that hereafter the Monthly Meetings of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Board be held on the third Wednesday of each month<span class='line-break'> </span>at 12 o'clock, noon.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committee'><u>Committee</u></span></p>
<p>The President not being present to announce the</p>

<p>The Schedule of Monthly Bills for February 14 was <span class='line-break'> </span>presented, showing a total of $4,463.49; and it was Voted<span class='line-break'> </span>that upon approval by the President, payment thereof<span class='line-break'> </span>be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Contract Perpetual Care'><u>Contract Perpetual Care</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Lots having recommended an ad<span class='line-break'></span>ditional contract of One Hundred dollars with Marquis<span class='line-break'> </span>R. Sweatt, for the perpetual care of Lot No. 5980, the<span class='line-break'> </span>same was approved by the Board.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report of Investments '><u>Report of Investments </u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Finance having presented a Report <span class='line-break'> </span>that no investments had been made on account of <span class='line-break'> </span>either the Repair Fund or the General Fund since Janu<span class='line-break'></span>ary 10, the date of the last meeting, it was voted that <span class='line-break'> </span>the same be accepted and placed on file.</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>361</p>
<p>by illness from further service, it was voted that he be dis<span class='line-break'></span>charged from the employ of the Corporation and that the sum<span class='line-break'> </span>of Three Hundred and Sixty ($360) dollars be paid to him as<span class='line-break'> </span>a gratuity, that being the amount of wages paid him for<span class='line-break'> </span>nine months of the year, which has been the limit of <span class='line-break'> </span>his recent employment.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Purchase of Land'><u>Purchase of Land</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the matter of the purchase of additional land <span class='line-break'> </span>for the purposes of the Corporation be referred to the Pres<span class='line-break'></span>ident and Mr. Watson as a Committee to investigate<span class='line-break'> </span>the same, and report to the Board at a future meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Maps of Cemetery'><u>Maps of Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the President be empowered to cause two<span class='line-break'> </span>suitable maps of the Cemetery to be prepared, one to <span class='line-break'> </span>be hung in the office at the Cemetery, and the other in <span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustee's room in the Boston office, and also to <span class='line-break'> </span>take such further action in regard to the preparation of <span class='line-break'> </span>other Maps of the Cemetery as he may deem advisable.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Current Bills to be paid'><u>Current Bills to be paid</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that as it is unlikely that a quorum will be <span class='line-break'> </span>present at meetings of the Board before September, <span class='line-break'> </span>the Treasurer be authorized to pay all current bills<span class='line-break'> </span>in the mean time, upon approval thereof by the Pres<span class='line-break'></span>ident.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Spruce Ave. Drainage of'><u>Spruce Ave. Drainage of</u></span></p>
<p>The Superintendent, as directed by the vote of the Board<span class='line-break'> </span>at the meeting of June 20, presented a report <sup>461</sup> upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the subject of the proper method of draining that <span class='line-break'> </span>portion of Spruce Avenue at the end of Acacia Path so<span class='line-break'> </span>as to prevent the accumulation of standing water at that<span class='line-break'> </span>point, and, after discussion of the different methods<span class='line-break'> </span>suggested in the report, it was voted that the desired <span class='line-break'> </span>result could best be obtained by tunnelling the hill<span class='line-break'> </span>from the junction of Spruce Avenue and Saffron Path <span class='line-break'> </span>to the stone drain in Law Avenue, thus permitting the <span class='line-break'> </span>surface water to descend by gravity through the tunnel<span class='line-break'> </span>and said stone drain in Lawn Avenue to the Charles River,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the President be authorized, in athe name and <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1137843">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 366)</a></h3>

<p>366</p>
<p>on behalf of the Corporation, to execute and deliver a<span class='line-break'> </span>contract for the necessary work at a cost not exceeding  <span class='line-break'> </span>Four Thousand dollars, the same to be in accordance <span class='line-break'> </span>with the Superintendent's plans and specifications.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Tomb charge waived, Lot 1209 for hollow Monument for Urns'><u>Tomb charge waived, Lot 1209 for hollow Monument for Urns</u></span></p>

Bowditch, esquire, for permission to erect on Lot No. 1209<span class='line-break'> </span>a hollow Monument for the reception of Urns containing <span class='line-break'> </span>the ashes of cremated bodies, but that before issuing  <span class='line-break'> </span>a permit for that purpose, he desired to know whether <span class='line-break'> </span>he should require the payment of the fee of Fifty dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>provided by the vote of the Board of Trustees passed May <span class='line-break'> </span>5, 1862.  Voted that, in view of the character of the <span class='line-break'> </span>proposed structure, the Superintendent be authorized to <span class='line-break'> </span>waive such payment, provided that in other respects the <span class='line-break'> </span>proposed erection was satisfactory to the Committee on Lots.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #4375 Petition of Alden E. Viles, Exr.'><u>Lot #4375 Petition of Alden E. Viles, Exr.</u></span></p>
<p>In the matter of the petition of Alden E. Viles, Executor of and <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustee under the will of Abram F. Rowe, formerly owner of Lot No.<span class='line-break'> </span>3=4325, now held by the Corporation in trust, asking for leave to remove<span class='line-break'> </span>from said Lot the Headsone erected by the said Abram F. Rowe<span class='line-break'> </span>to the memory of his first wife, and to replace it by a larger <span class='line-break'> </span>and better granite Monument, which was referred to the President<span class='line-break'> </span>with power, the President reported that he had granted leave to <span class='line-break'> </span>erect the proposed Monument, upon the condition that the said<span class='line-break'> </span>Headstone be removed from the Lot but that it be buried <span class='line-break'> </span>therein, so that in case any request should be hereafter made<span class='line-break'> </span>that it be replaced upon the Lot, it might e in teh power <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board to order that this be done, if they should deem it<span class='line-break'> </span>advisable.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Vesper Lot Request for P. C. of Grave'><u>Vesper Lot Request for P. C. of Grave</u></span></p>
<p>In the matter of the request of Mrs E. J. A. Higgins to be <span class='line-break'> </span>allowed to deposit a sum of money sufficient to provide for <span class='line-break'> </span>the perpetual care of a Grave in Vesper Lot, in which she is <span class='line-break'> </span>interested, which was referred to the President to investigate<span class='line-break'> </span>the same and report at this meeting, the President reported<span class='line-break'> </span>that the charter of the Corporation gives it power to make con<span class='line-break'></span>tracts for perpetual care with the owners of Lots only, and <span class='line-break'> </span>that, as the purchaser of a grave acquires merely an easement,<span class='line-break'> </span>with no property rights, the Corporation has no authority to <span class='line-break'> </span>make a contract with him for the care of it.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Improvements at Cemetery'><u>Improvements at Cemetery</u></span></p>
<p>In the matter of certain needed improvements at the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery, which were detailed at length at the last meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>and in regard to which the President was requested to report</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137855">
<h3><a name="page-1137855">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 369)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>369</p>
<p>at the present meeting, stating the order in which such im<span class='line-break'></span>provements should be taken up and carried out, the President <span class='line-break'> </span>reported that the following work was all that could conveniently <span class='line-break'> </span>be done during the next year: 1. The enlargment of the catacombs<span class='line-break'> </span>in the Receiving Tomb; 2. The building of a potting shed for <span class='line-break'> </span>the Greenhouse; and, 3. The erection of a house for the care <span class='line-break'> </span>of half-hardy plants.  The next improvement to follow <span class='line-break'> </span>these he thought should be a new Pumping Station, and stated <span class='line-break'> </span>that plans and estimates for all the work proposed would<span class='line-break'> </span>be made before the net Annual Meeting of the Proprietors, so <span class='line-break'> </span>that the same can be presented to the Trustees at their first<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting thereafter.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Work at Cemetery authorized'><u>Work at Cemetery authorized</u></span></p>
<p>The President further stated that he had taken the responsi<span class='line-break'></span>bility of having the plastering removed from the walls of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Ladies' Waiting Room in the Administration Building and replaced <span class='line-break'> </span>by plastering laid upon wire lathing at about one inch from <span class='line-break'> </span>the brick for the purpose of preventing the leakage which <span class='line-break'> </span>formerly occurred there, and that, after a recent violent rain<span class='line-break'> </span>storm, there had been no appearance of such leakage;<span class='line-break'> </span>also, that he had authorized the Superintendent to lay six<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred feet of 8-inch water pipe in Fountain Avenue,<span class='line-break'> </span>thus completing the Main to the Engine House, the estim<span class='line-break'></span>ated expense thereof being less than One Thousand dollars.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Henry H. Fay Request'><u>Henry H. Fay Request</u></span></p>
<p>The President further reported in the matter of the request <span class='line-break'> </span>of Henry H. Fay in regard to a proposed contract for the <span class='line-break'> </span>care of Lot No. 1416, without guaranty, which had been <span class='line-break'> </span>referred to Mr. Hutchins and himself, as a Committee</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137859">
<h3><a name="page-1137859">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 370)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>370</p>
<p>to investigate the subject and report, that they had [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>considered the same, and had endeavored to arrange a <span class='line-break'> </span>meeting with Mr. Fay, but without success; they intended, <span class='line-break'> </span>however, to take up the matter again at an early day,<span class='line-break'> </span>and would make a further effort to meet Mr. Fay and<span class='line-break'> </span>go over it with him.</p>
<p><u>Dissolved.</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='November 21 Meeting'><u>November 21 Meeting</u></span></p>

<p>The Monthly Meeting of the Board of Trustees was held, as<span class='line-break'> </span>notified, on Wednesday, November 21, 1906, at 12 o'clock, noon.<span class='line-break'> </span>Present, the President and Messrs. Beal, Cheever, Choate, <span class='line-break'> </span>Foster, Hemenway, Hobbs, Hutchins, Jones, Russell and Watson.</p>

<p>371</p>
<p>October 17, the date of the last meeting, it was voted that<span class='line-break'> </span>the same be accepted and placed on file.</p>

<p>The schedule of the Monthly Bills for November 21, was <span class='line-break'> </span>presented, showing a total of $6,565.96, and it was voted<span class='line-break'> </span>that upon approval by the President, payment thereof<span class='line-break'> </span>be made by the Treasurer.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Eliza J. Levy Request granted'><u>Eliza J. Levy Request granted</u></span></p>
<p>Upon the request of Eliza J. Levy for a re-conveyance to herself<span class='line-break'> </span>of Lot No. 5918, re-conveyed by her to the Corporation in trust, <span class='line-break'> </span>July 8, 1892, it was voted that she be allowed to sell said<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot upon terms satisfactory to the Board of Trustees.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Changes in Cremation Law'><u>Changes in Cremation Law</u></span></p>
<p>Voted that the President be authorized to petition the Legis<span class='line-break'></span>lature, or join with others in so doing for such changes in <span class='line-break'> </span>the laws relating to cremation as may seem to him desirable.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Chas. P. Bowditch Monument on Lot 1208 authorized'><u>Chas. P. Bowditch Monument on Lot 1208 authorized</u></span></p>

No. 1208, a hollow Monument for the reception <span class='line-break'> </span>of urns containing the ashes of cremated bodies, substan<span class='line-break'></span>tially in accordance with plans and drawings pre<span class='line-break'></span>sented by him, the details of said structure to be satis<span class='line-break'></span>factory to the President and Superintendent.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasurer authorized to sell stock held as collateral'><u>Treasurer authorized to sell stock held as collateral</u></span></p>
<p>Voted, that the Treasurer be, and he hereby is, authorized, <span class='line-break'> </span>with the approval of one of the members of the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Finance, to sell, assign and transfer One Hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>shares of the capital stock of the American Telephone<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; Telegraph Company, pledged to the Corporation by Mr.<span class='line-break'> </span>Henry B. Williams as additional security for a loan on <span class='line-break'> </span>mortage of real estate in Newton.   <u>Dissolved</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

Not only have his opinion been much <span class='line-break'> </span>deferred tto in all mattters relating to the public health, but to <span class='line-break'> </span>all business questions he brought a ripe judgement and sense <span class='line-break'> </span>of responsibility that won the respect of his associates. He <span class='line-break'> </span>was unremitting in attendance att meetings of the Board, was <span class='line-break'> </span>independent and outspoken wihtout discourtesy and was <span class='line-break'> </span>considerate of corporate interests without forgetting what is <span class='line-break'> </span>due the public; and the Board Keenly regret the loss of one <span class='line-break'> </span>who so long has proved himself a prudent adviser and <span class='line-break'> </span>faithful friend. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Lot No. 1384]  A petition was recieved from Arthur J. <p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot No. 1384 Petition of Arthur J. Meriam'><u>Lot No. 1384 Petition of Arthur J. Meriam</u></span></p>
<p>The President on behalf of the Committee on Lots reported that<span class='line-break'> </span>the petition of Arthur J. Meriam was based upon the fact that<span class='line-break'> </span>his father, Jonas Meriam, had an equitable interest in a part of<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot No. 1384, which was deeded to Thomas Mair and was after-</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='S-'>S-</span></p>
<p>wards deeded back to the Corporation by said Mair without<span class='line-break'> </span>mention of the Meriam interest, and that the evidence satis<span class='line-break'></span>fied the Committee <u>prima facie</u> that Jonas Meriam had such<span class='line-break'> </span>interest in fact in part of said Lot, as indicated by a <span class='line-break'> </span>stone bound on the same, this view being substantiatied by a<span class='line-break'> </span>written statement of Caroline E. Skinner, sole surviving heir<span class='line-break'> </span>of said Thomas Mair, who joins in said petition; and that<span class='line-break'> </span>upon these facts the Committee, to whom the petition was<span class='line-break'> </span>referred with power, passed the following vote:</p>
<p>Voted, that, until otherwise ordered by the Board of Trustees,<span class='line-break'> </span>permission be given for the burial of the widow and de<span class='line-break'></span>scendants of said Jonas Meriam in the part of Lot No.<span class='line-break'> </span>1384, claimed to have belonged to him equitably, as long<span class='line-break'> </span>as vacant graves therein remain unoccupied, and<span class='line-break'> </span>upon this report it was voted that same be entered<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the records of the Trustees.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Storage House for Half-hardy Plants &amp;c'><u>Storage House for Half-hardy Plants &amp;c</u></span></p>
<p>The President then gave notice that at the next meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board he should ask for an appropriation not ex<span class='line-break'> </span>ceeding Four Thousand dollars to be used for the erection<span class='line-break'> </span>of a storage house for half-hardy plants and a small<span class='line-break'> </span>greenhouse for the propogation of trees and shrubs.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Henry H. Fay appears in support of Request'><u>Henry H. Fay appears in support of Request</u></span></p>
<p>Pursuant to the vote passed at the meeting of January<span class='line-break'> </span>9, Mr Henry H. Fay appeared before the Board and<span class='line-break'> </span>presented arguments in support of his request that sepa<span class='line-break'> </span>rate accounts be kept with the several proprietors of<span class='line-break'> </span>Lots under perpetual care, and that any surplus of<span class='line-break'> </span>annual income be applied to the care and restoration<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Monuments and Headstones on said Lots.</p>
<p>After hearing Mr. Fay's remarks, the President re<span class='line-break'></span>plied that there were in the minds of the Board three<span class='line-break'> </span>definite and specific reasons why his request should<span class='line-break'> </span>not be granted: first, that it was a serious question<span class='line-break'> </span>whether the corporation wished to bind itself to keep<span class='line-break'> </span>separate ledger accounts with Lot owners perpetually<span class='line-break'> </span>second, that for two generations there has been inserted<span class='line-break'> </span>in the contracts for the care of Lots a provision that<span class='line-break'> </span>any surplus of income shall be expended for the general<span class='line-break'> </span>purposes of the Cemetery; and, third, that as a charge of<span class='line-break'> </span>Fifteen dollars is made for the care of a Headstone<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the assumption that it will last for about eighty<span class='line-break'> </span>years, the result of the adoption of the plan proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>by Mr. Fay would be that many Lot owners would decide to</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137917">
<h3><a name="page-1137917">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 385)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>385</p>
<p>take the chances and not pay this amount and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>revenues of the Corporation would be proportionally dimin<span class='line-break'></span>ished. The subject having been fully discussed later<span class='line-break'> </span>in the meeting, it was voted that the President commu<span class='line-break'></span>nicate with Mr. Fay and inform him courteously that the<span class='line-break'> </span>Board had given the matter of his request their careful<span class='line-break'> </span>consideration and had concluded that it was inex<span class='line-break'></span>pedient to grant the same.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Henry M. Warren Request Lot No. 3744'><u>Henry M. Warren Request Lot No. 3744</u></span></p>
<p>A request was<sup>470</sup> received from Henry M. Warren, es<span class='line-break'></span>quire, of Philadelphia, for permission to place upon Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>No. 3744, owned by his father, Bishop Warren, of Denver,<span class='line-break'> </span>Colorado, a granite Sarcophagus, having a base of<span class='line-break'> </span>seven feet, three inches, by four feet, two inches, with<span class='line-break'> </span>a height of four feet, The reasons given in sup<span class='line-break'></span>port of this request were that although the stone was<span class='line-break'> </span>a large one for a Lot of this size, a considerable portion<span class='line-break'> </span>was the base stone and not prominent, and that the<span class='line-break'> </span>stone was low in effect, which was emphasized by the<span class='line-break'> </span>steep bank which rises some ten or twelve feet<span class='line-break'> </span>immediately in the rear of the spot where it is intended<span class='line-break'> </span>that the stone be placed; and also that the locality<span class='line-break'> </span>was a retired one and there was no other Monuments<span class='line-break'> </span>near. Voted that the subject be referred to the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots, with power.</p>
<p>Dissolved<span class='line-break'> </span>Lewis G. Farmer,<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary.</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Oath of Secretary'><u>Oath of Secretary</u></span></p>
<p>Commonwealth of Massachusetts<span class='line-break'> </span>Suffolk, S.S. Boston <date when='1907-04-17'>April 17, 1907.</date></p>
<p>Personally appeared John L. Dill and made oath<span class='line-break'> </span>that he would faithfully and impartially, discharge the duties<span class='line-break'> </span>of Secretary pro-tempore, of the Proprietors of the Cemetery of<span class='line-break'> </span>Mount Auburn, before me</p>
<p>Jerome Jones. Justice of the peace.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='April 17 Meeting'><u>April 17 Meeting</u></span></p>
<p><date when='1907-04-17'>April 17<sup>th</sup> 1907.</date></p>
<p>The monthly meeting of the Board of Trustees was held as notified,<span class='line-break'> </span>on Wednesday April 17, 1907, at 12 O'Clock noon. Present the<span class='line-break'> </span>President, and Messrs. Choate, Foster, Richardson, Jones,<span class='line-break'> </span>Beal, Whitney, Russell and Hemenway.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secretary pro. tempore'><u>Secretary pro. tempore</u></span></p>
<p>In the absence of the Secretary, John L. Dill, was chosen<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary of the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mt. Auburn pro tempore</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records'><u>Records</u></span></p>
<p>The Records of the meeting of. March. 20<sup>th</sup> were read and approved.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='half-hardy storage House.'><u>half-hardy storage House.</u></span></p>
<p>In accordance with the notice given at the last meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>the President asked for an appropriation of Four Thousand dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>to be expended for the erection of a Storage house for half hardy<span class='line-break'> </span>plants, and a small Greenhouse for the propagation of trees<span class='line-break'> </span>and shrubs, and it was Voted that the appropriation be granted.</p>

<div id="page-1137925">
<h3><a name="page-1137925">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 387)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>387</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot #3744 - petition of Henry M. Warren'><u>Lot <sup>#</sup>3744 - petition of Henry M. Warren</u></span></p>
<p>The Committee on Lots<sup>471</sup>, to whom was referred with power the Petition of<span class='line-break'> </span>Henry M. Warren, in behalf of his father, Bishop Warren of Denver Col.<span class='line-break'> </span>owner of lot No 3744, for leave to place thereon, a monument, larger<span class='line-break'> </span>than permitted by the General rules. Report that they decided to grant<span class='line-break'> </span>the request. The rule is intended to prevent injury to adjoining lots,<span class='line-break'> </span>by monuments of a size that would dwarf neighboring monuments,<span class='line-break'> </span>but for reasons set forth in the Peititon, which the committee found<span class='line-break'> </span>to be in accordance with fact, no such injury would be done<span class='line-break'> </span>in this case. Under such circumstances the committee deemed it<span class='line-break'> </span>just and rearmable that the lot owner be gratified.</p>
<p>Voted: That Representatives be designated for lots, as follows</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Representatives appointed'><u>Representatives appointed</u></span></p>
<p><sup>#</sup>2484 Lester M. Dorr. of Newton Mass. Son<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>#</sup>2802 Sarah. Elizabeth Hyde " Cambridge Mass. daughter<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>#</sup>4479 Everett Flint Damon " Boston Mass. Grand-Son<span class='line-break'> </span><sup>#</sup>5506 Helen S. Jones " Brookline Mass- Widow</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Monthly bills'><u>Monthly bills</u></span></p>
<p>The Schedule of Monthly bills for April 17, was presented<span class='line-break'> </span>showing a total of <sup>$</sup>7032.03, and it was Voted that<span class='line-break'> </span>upon approval by the President, payment thereof be made<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Treasurer.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1137947">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 396)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>1907<span class='line-break'> </span>[Alterations to] In accordance with the notice given at the last<span class='line-break'> </span>[Receiving Tomb] meeting the President asked for an appropriation<span class='line-break'> </span>of Fifteen Hundred dollars to be expended in making<span class='line-break'> </span>[Appropriation] the required alterations in the Receiving Tomb, and <span class='line-break'> </span>[Voted] it was Voted that the appropriation be granted<span class='line-break'> </span>[Storage House] The President then gave notice that at the <span class='line-break'> </span>[for Healf-Hardy] next meeting of the Baord he should ask for <span class='line-break'> </span>[Plants, +c.] an appropriation not exceeding Four Thousand <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars to be used for the erection of a storage <span class='line-break'> </span>house for half-hardy plants and a sunce<span class='line-break'> </span>greenhouse for the propagation of trees and shrubs. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Henry H. Fay] Pursuant to the  vote passed at the meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>[appears in] of January 8, Mr. Henry H. Fay appeared before <span class='line-break'> </span>[support of] the Board and presented arguments in sup<span class='line-break'></span>[request] port of his request that separate accounts be <span class='line-break'> </span>kept with the several proprietors of Lot under <span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care and that any surplus of <span class='line-break'> </span>annual income be applied to the care under<span class='line-break'> </span>restoration of the Monuments and Steadstones<span class='line-break'> </span>on said Lots. After hearing Mr. Fay's remarks<span class='line-break'> </span>the President replied that there were in the <span class='line-break'> </span>minds of the Board three definite and specific <span class='line-break'> </span>masons why his request not be granted. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137949">
<h3><a name="page-1137949">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 397)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>first, that it was a serious question whether the <span class='line-break'> </span>corporation wished to bind itself to keep separate<span class='line-break'> </span>ledger accounts with Lot owners perpetually: <span class='line-break'> </span>Second that for two generations there has been <span class='line-break'> </span>inserted in the contracts for the care of Lots a <span class='line-break'> </span>provision that any surplus of income shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be expended for the general purpose of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery: and third that as a charge of Fifteen<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars is made for the care of a Headstone<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the assumption that it will last for<span class='line-break'> </span>about eighty years the result of the adoption<span class='line-break'> </span>of the plan proposed by Mr. Fay would be <span class='line-break'> </span>that many Lot owners would decide to take Mr. Mances + not pay this <span class='line-break'> </span>amount, and that the revenues of the corpora<span class='line-break'></span>tion would be proporationally diminished. <span class='line-break'> </span>The subject having been fully discussed later in <span class='line-break'> </span>the meeting it was voted that the President <span class='line-break'> </span>communicate with Mr. Fay and inform him<span class='line-break'> </span>courteously that the Board had given the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>of his request this careful consideration<span class='line-break'> </span>and had concluded that it was inexpedient to <span class='line-break'> </span>grant the same. <span class='line-break'> </span>[Henry M. Warren] A request was received from Henry M. Warren </p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1137951">
<h3><a name="page-1137951">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 398)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Vol. 7 - Trustee Minutes 2 of 3</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1137953">
<h3><a name="page-1137953">Trustees Records, Vol. 7, 1886 (page 399)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>3/</p>
<p>esquire, of Philadelphia, for permission to place<span class='line-break'> </span>upon Lot No. 3744, owned by his father, Bishop<span class='line-break'> </span>Warren, of Denver, Colorado, a granite Sarcophagus<span class='line-break'> </span>having a base of seven feet, three inches by four<span class='line-break'> </span>feet, two inches, with a height of four feet. The<span class='line-break'> </span>reasons given in support of this request, were<span class='line-break'> </span>that although the stone was a large one for a<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot of this size, <del>the base stone covered a much larger<span class='line-break'> </span>area that the bulk presented to the eye above it</del> a considerable portion was the base stone<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; not prominent, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the stone was low in effect, which was empha<span class='line-break'></span>sized by the steep bank which rises some ten or<span class='line-break'> </span>twelve feet immediately in the rear of the spot<span class='line-break'> </span>where it is intended that the stone be placed, and<span class='line-break'> </span>also that the locality was retired one and there<span class='line-break'> </span>were no other monuments near. Voted that the<span class='line-break'> </span>subject be referred to the Committee on Lots,<span class='line-break'> </span>with power.</p>
</div>
</div>
